Ninth, White Simplicity Flying Dragon—*Oral Instructions* say this is white quartz.
Tenth, Luminous Jade Spirit Vermilion—*Oral Instructions* say this is true cinnabar, which attracts mustard seeds.
Eleventh, Five Essences Metal Ram—*Oral Instructions* say this is actinolite.
Twelfth, Cloud Flower Flying Petal—*Oral Instructions* say this is mica, radiant and translucent.
Thirteenth, Flowing Cinnabar Sun-Grease—*Oral Instructions* say this is lead white.
Fourteenth, Solitary Peak Lone-Born—*Oral Instructions* say this is clove, with its pungent flavor.
Fifteenth, Azure Mound Patterned Marquis—*Oral Instructions* say this is azurite.
Sixteenth, Reverse-Walking Spirit Bone—*Oral Instructions* say this is halite.
Seventeenth, White Tiger Shed Tooth—*Oral Instructions* say this is gold-tooth stone.
Eighteenth, Nine Spirits Yellow Youth—*Oral Instructions* say this is sulfur.
Nineteenth, Land Void Remnant Life—*Oral Instructions* say this is dragon bone, best when it adheres to the tongue.
Twentieth, Majestic Pattern Central King—*Oral Instructions* say this is tiger brain.
Twenty-First, Submerged Brilliance Converging Radiance—*Oral Instructions* say this is pearl from within a clam.
Twenty-Second, Zhangyang Feather Mystery—*Oral Instructions* say this is white aconite.
Twenty-Third, Green Hidden Stone Mother—*Oral Instructions* say this is magnetite.
Twenty-Fourth, Central Mountain Abundant Fat—*Oral Instructions* say this is *Taiyi*’s remnant root, taking the yellow from its center.

These twenty-four ingredients combine to form the Eight Radiant, Four-Blossomed, Five-Pearled, Crimson-Born Spirit Elixir. Ingesting one *liang* of this elixir will cause nine morning lights to sprout from the head, the face to bear jade radiance, and flying reflections of precious luminosity to illuminate all beneath heaven. One will ascend to the Purple Void, enter and exit the Jade Purity, and repose in the Morning Chamber.

The *Supreme One’s Numinous Elixir of Cloud-Petal Jade Dust* states: The flourishing fruit is the bright pearl of spring’s awakening. Sesame is the profound numen of autumn’s clarity. Cinnabar jujube is the cloud fungus of flourishing yang. Poria is the crimson dawn’s hidden embryo. When the five flowers merge with mist and the three qi refine the essence, the six qi are harmonized, the hun-souls nurtured, and the spirit guarded. Those who obtain this method will become Heavenly Immortals, their aged white returning to the mysterious, their infant visage restored, their countenance that of a youth. A thousand harms will not assail them, and their lifespan will extend ten thousand years.

It further states: The method of the Mystic Water Cloud-Essence Elixir is also called the Vermilion Essence of Flourishing Clouds. Consuming five *ge* daily will make the body fragrant and the face bear the radiance of youth—this is a divine transcendence method.

It further states: The Supreme One’s Four Guardians Pill generates spirit in the five viscera, guards the six bones, nourishes the seven orifices, harmonizes the nine barriers, refines the three hun-souls, brightens the two pupils, preserves the one body, and grants longevity of ten thousand years.

It further states: The Three Spirits Dragon Bone benefits the six fluids, nourishes the nine intestines, and halts the whitening of black hair.

The Supreme One’s Pill and Powder Method of Sweet Flag states: It guards the center and refines the spirit, granting longevity and enduring vision, filling and congealing the bone marrow, replenishing the brain’s blood. With prolonged consumption, the complexion becomes purple like that of a young maiden. Another name is Nine Cycles of Primordial Essence. Sweet flag is also called the *changyang* numinous herb.

All the above are drawn from the *Inner Instructions of the Supreme Purity’s Nine Perfected* as their foundation.

The *True Scripture of the Great Cavern* contains the Nine Cycles Frost Snow, Jade-Tooth Flower Elixir, Returning White Jade Mystic Water, Flowing Gold Liquid Essence, Jade Grove Congealed Flower, Sun-Moon Water—all methods for ascending to heaven in broad daylight as a flying immortal.

It further states: The Immortal Mother’s Gold Elixir, also called the Queen Mother of the West’s Age-Halting, Old-Age-Reversing Flying Elixir, grants immortality to those who consume it, their faces bearing the youthful countenance of a maiden.

The *Scripture of Purple Radiance and Blazing Light* states: The Flying Elixir’s purple flower and flowing essence possess a hundred shifting hues.

It further states: The ointment of jade embryo and jasper liquid.

The *Scripture of Flying and Soaring Feathers* states: The ointment of refined gold essence—consuming a single mouthful grants a lifespan of seventy thousand years.

The *Supreme Scripture of the Great Ultimate Lord’s Guarding Life and the Five Viscera* states: The cloud herb of mysterious clarity is the fat of black sesame, also called Mystic Clarity. The blossoming nectar of herbs is white honey. The five lights and seven whites of numinous vegetables are Chinese chives. White Simplicity Flying Dragon is white quartz, also found in the *Nine Perfected’s Inner Instructions*.

The *Arrayed Records of the Latter Sage Dao Lord* states: The Jade-Tooth Flower Elixir is a medicinal species. Crimson Mound Vermilion Child, ten *jin*—*Oral Instructions* say this is cinnabar. Cinnabar Mountain Sun-Soul, five *jin*—*Oral Instructions* say this is realgar. White Simplicity Flying Dragon, one *jin*—*Oral Instructions* say this is white quartz. Azure Essence Jade Maiden, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is malachite. Purple Mound Patterned Marquis, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is purple quartz. Azure City Flying Flower, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is azurite. Northern Emperor Mystic Vermilion, one *jin*—*Oral Instructions* say this is saltpeter. Nine Spirits Yellow Youth, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is sulfur. Five Essences Metal Ram, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is actinolite. Cloud Flower Flying Petal, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is mica.

White Tiger Shedding Teeth, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is gold-tooth stone. Flowing Cinnabar White Cream, one *jin*—*Oral Instructions* say this is lead powder. Reversing Spirit Bone, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is halite. Dark Terrace Moon Essence, five *liang*—*Oral Instructions* say this is orpiment.

Together these fourteen flowering elixirs, when refined into one *liang*, become One Immortal. White Flower has one name: *Zhangju*; one name: *Zhangming*; one name: *Zhangsheng*; one name: *Zhangcao*; one name: *Zhanglu*; one name: *Tongshen*; one name: *Tongjing*; one name: *Tongling*; one name: *Royal Maiden*; one name: *Household Immortal*; one name: *Household Treasure*; one name: *Household Zhi*; one name: *Extending Life*; one name: *Longevity Herb*; one name: *Guardian of the Palace*; one name: *Guardian of the Homestead*. The Twelve Divisions have one name: *Night Call*; one name: *Night Cry*; one name: *Inducing Essence*; one name: *Yang Brightness*; one name: *Yin Brightness*; one name: *Red Kudzu*; one name: *Danglu*.

Altogether twenty-four names, corresponding above to the twenty-four qi of Heaven and Earth. Ingesting a *fangcun*-spoonful enables communion with spirits and attracts fortune.

*The Esoteric Transmission of Wen Shi* states: Laozi, traveling east with the Pass Keeper, ascended the Sun Cavern’s Ever-Bright Mountain, plucked the cinnabar mulberries of Fusang, and scattered the vermilion blossoms of the forest like stars.

*The Fourth Scroll of Daoist Biographies* states: Jiaozhi produced the cinnabar gathered by Ge Hong. The fourteenth scroll records: Shuang Xizu, styled Zhongyuan, during the fourteenth year of Liang Emperor Wu’s *Tianjian* era, personally journeyed to Wuling to seek cinnabar. He distributed both public and private funds, amounting to several tens of *jin* of gold, all to relieve the destitute.

**Elixir Furnaces and Incense Burners**

*The Fourteenth Scroll of the Cavernous Spirit Canon* states: When ingesting cinnabar and burning incense, use five incense burners. *The Scripture of Great Cavern True Script, Zhi Elixir, Azure Jade Burner, and Refined Root of Supple Vajra* also appears in *The Arrayed Records of the Three Heavenly Lords of Highest Clarity*.

*The Concealed Instructions for Ascending Perfection* states: Regarding the incense burner for burning incense, no one describes its form or mold. The ancients often used *boshan* burners and tripods. *The Eight Mighties’ Dragon-Summoning Scripture* mentions the *boshan* incense burner.

*The Upper Scroll of the Great Perfection Regulations* states: The Lofty Mystery Terrace has a great incense burner, five *chi* in height, perpetually burning incense without the smoke ever ceasing.

*The Sixth Scroll of the Scripture of Ascending Mystery* states: Jade lads scatter wondrous blossoms; jade maidens present the incense burner. The third scroll states: The Seven Treasures Terrace has a seven-jeweled incense burner, burning myriad wondrous incenses, their fragrance suffusing boundlessly.

*The Third Scroll of the Scripture of the Ocean of Emptiness* states: At that time, the Ocean of Emptiness’ Wisdom Treasury arose, adjusted his robe at his seat, held the incense burner, stood reverently facing the Heavenly Worthy, his gaze unwavering, his mind free of distraction.

*The Upper Scripture of Astronomy* states: The sun and moon hang their radiance; the golden burner stands lofty—sometimes at the Gate of Separation, sometimes in the Palace of Destiny.

*The True Scripture of the Eight Simplicities* states: Immortals know only how to fly elixirs and summon frost, to smelt cinnabar clouds, to dissolve gold with water-jade, and to blaze the nine furnaces to the heavens.

*The Tenth Scroll of Daoist Biographies* states: Dongxiang Zongchao, styled Yilun, was a native of Qianzou in Gaomi. Once, while performing the Dao at an open-air altar, the incense in the censer suddenly overflowed when the *lian* note sounded. Again, though no fire burned in the burner, smoke arose of its own accord, filling the space and lingering long without dissipating.

The fourteenth scroll records: Shuang Xizu, styled Zhongyuan, lived during the Liang dynasty. Fond of reading scriptures, he never let them leave his hands. When the Marquis of Linru was appointed as the Pure Envoy to Jingzhou, his attendants placed an incense burner before Xizu and departed without a word.

The fifteenth scroll states: Tao Hongjing sealed the Three True Treasure Scriptures in a tin casket and cast them into a cliffside cavern. He also placed a pure gold magpie-tailed incense burner beside the scriptures for their veneration.

The twentieth scroll states: The Daoist nun Song Yuxian was a native of Shanyin in Kuaiji. Though born a woman, her resolve was not her own. When she reached marriageable age, her parents betrothed her to the Xu family. Secretly, she prepared ritual garments. Upon arriving at her husband’s home, during the Six Rites, she donned a yellow cloth skirt and coarse hemp robe, held a magpie-tailed incense burner, and refused to partake in the wedding rites. The guests and hosts were astonished, but the husband’s family could not compel her. She was cast out and returned home, thus becoming a renunciate.

*The Upper Scripture of the Great Kalpa* states: Heavenly maidens hold the fragrant trays of the Net of Heaven, bearing jade burners, burning the incense of the Nine Harmonies.

*Volume Four of the Three Caverns’ Pearl Satchel* concludes.
*Volume Five of the Three Caverns’ Pearl Satchel* begins.

The *Sitting-in-Forgetfulness and Refined Contemplation* by Wang Xuanhe, the Feathered Guest of the Vast Sea of Lu in the Great Tang

The *Nanhua [Zhuangzi]*, "On the Equality of Things, Second Chapter," states: Nan Guo Ziqi leaned against his armrest and sat, gazing upward and exhaling with a sigh, as if he had lost his counterpart. The sixth chapter says: Cast off the limbs, dim the hearing and sight, depart from form and abandon knowledge, merging with the Great Thoroughfare—this is called sitting-in-forgetfulness. The fourth chapter says: Maim the form, and one will not be conscripted for labor; how much more so if one maims their virtue? It also says: Do not listen with the ears, do not listen with the heart, but listen with qi. Qi is emptiness awaiting things. When the empty chamber generates brightness, auspiciousness abides therein.

*The Second Transmission of Daoist Learning* states: Master Zhang the Celestial Master roamed the Five Peaks, refining his contemplation and accumulating resonance. The Perfected descended, and the Dao was accomplished, earning him the title Celestial Master.

Volume Five cites *Records of Assembled Immortals*: Liu Ningzhi, styled Zhi’an, with the childhood name Longevity, was a native of Zhijiang in Nanjun. Devoted to the Dao with diligent progress, in the fourteenth year of Yuanjia, while in refined contemplation, he suddenly felt a sharp pain on his forehead. Scratching it, he obtained nine precious pearls, which he floated in clear water, illuminating the entire chamber. At that time, the Prince of Linchuan was stationed in Jiangling and sought to see the pearls, so Liu gave three to his messenger.

*The Scripture of Daoist Traces* states: The Green Lad said: In refined contemplation, one must first burn incense to the left and right.

*The Upper Clarity Scripture of the Eight Effulgences* says: Refine contemplation for a hundred days, and Perfected Ones will descend in form. Immortals will visit your chamber, converse with you, bestow upon you the elixir of transcendence, and transmit to you the Way of the Divine Perfected.

*Preface to the Scripture of the Five Thousand Characters by Lord Ge the Immortal* says: Through refined contemplation and distant resonance, the Supreme Dao Lord dispatched Perfected Ones to bestow the *Scripture of the Five Thousand Characters* upon Emperor Wen, its subtleties profound. It also says: In tranquil contemplation, awaiting the Perfected, the myriad wonders converge in response. Inwardly observing one’s form and shadow, spirit and qi endure long. When the body harmonizes with the Dao and virtue, the ten thousand spirits tremble in submission, calamities vanish in the Nine Yin, blessings arise in the Ten Directions, and the nation and family are at peace—who can fathom this?

The *Zhuangzi*, "The Great Master" chapter, says: Sitting-in-forgetfulness means casting off the limbs, dimming hearing and sight, departing from form and abandoning knowledge, merging with the Great Thoroughfare. This is also the meaning of refined contemplation.

The *Nanhua Treatise*, "On the Equality of Things," also says: Nan Guo Ziqi leaned against his armrest and sat, sighing as if he had lost his counterpart. Thus, his movements were like dragging withered wood, and his sitting was like a heap of dead ashes. This, too, is the meaning of refined contemplation.

*The Hidden Instructions for Ascending to Perfection* states: The Daoist of the Five Spirits, Zhi Ziyuan, in a quiet chamber refined his contemplation, visualizing the Five Stars above his head: Jupiter on the left, Venus on the right, Mars at his knees, and Saturn in his heart, each emitting radiant qi and color. Practicing this for a long time, whether going out or traveling afar, he never forgot to contemplate, and nothing could withstand him. These five spirits, when united with the human body, enable one to ascend to heaven in broad daylight.

*The Inner Transmission of Lord Pei* states: The Buddhist Daoist Zhi Ziyuan received from Lord Pei the inner arts of longevity. It also says: Seeking herbs and refined contemplation, though both lead to the Dao along the same stream, differ in their origins. Ingesting herbs preserves the form, and when the form is sound, the spirit is at peace. Refined contemplation pacifies the spirit, and when the spirit is unimpeded, the form is preserved. These two principles mutually support each other, yet there are grades of superiority. Now, fearing the spirit’s leakage while the form is abandoned, refined contemplation is deemed superior. No one has seen the form depart while the spirit remains, so ingesting herbs is considered inferior. Those who attain the Dao through one practice alone also reach the shore of the Way, yet it is not as perfect as combining both, allowing herbs and contemplation to work in tandem, form and spirit to merge. Then, like adding fuel to extend the day, the blade moves without obstruction, the course of life is naturally established, and the realm of death cannot arise.

*The Fifth [Scroll] of True Reports* says: Ordinary people should constantly visualize their own form in refined contemplation, making it as vivid as possible, appearing before them. Have the light of the sun and moon perpetually shine upon the face, illuminating the entire form, with the sun on the left and the moon on the right, nine inches before the face. Once the visualization is complete, click the teeth three times and softly recite: "The Primordial Womb’s Upper Perfected, Twin Effulgences of the Three Mysteries, restrain the seven po on the right, bind the three hun on the left, so that my spirit and luminosity may abide with my form forever." Afterward, click the teeth twenty-one times and swallow saliva twenty-one times. This is called the Way of the August Lord’s Recording of Form and Binding of the Hun, enabling one to become a spiritually luminous immortal and live forever without dying. If one cannot recite the incantation, visualization alone is also permissible.

*The Seventh [Scroll] of True Reports* states: The Immortal Zhang Weizi was the daughter of Zhang Qing from the time of Emperor Zhao of Han. Once, in quiet seclusion, she refined her contemplation with sincere devotion, and the Jade Consort of Eastern Florescence from the Eastern Sea, Ting Wenqi, descended to her, bestowing the Way of Ingesting Mist. The method of ingesting mist originated from this.

It also says: Ping Zhongjie of Kuocang Mountain, a Daoist from Hedong, received from his master, Master Song, the Way of the Heart-Mirror. After forty-five years of such practice, his refined contemplation made his body grow younger, and his form possessed true qi. The Central Yellow Elder dispatched an envoy to welcome him, and he ascended to heaven in broad daylight, riding clouds and dragons. He now resides in the Cloud Terrace of Canglang.

It also says: Fan Boci, a native of Guiyang, entered Tianmu Mountain to ingest herbs and consume sesame. After seventeen years of refined contemplation, the Supreme Perfected Lord of Life and Destiny descended and bestowed thirty-six scrolls of scriptures. Later, he ingested the returning elixir and ascended to heaven in broad daylight, now known as the Perfected of the Mysterious Unity.

*The Records of the Golden Perfected of the Great One* states: Once, Lord Pei resided on Kongtong Mountain, cultivating refined contemplation. In the first year, his form became faint and indistinct. In the second year, the Five Thearchs rode the sun, their forms appearing at his left and right.

In the third year, he laughed and played in joy throughout the day. In the fifth year, the Five Thearchs and the Sun Lords then accompanied Lord Pei in riding the flying dragon chariot, journeying east to the Heaven of the Sun’s Cavern, the Palace of Fusang on the Eastern Mengchang Long Mound, the City of the Eight Poles. They ascended the Terrace of Illuminating Perfection, sat in the Hall of Sparse Forest, and were bestowed the Nine Talismans of the Wielding Spirit and the Symbols of the Nine Provinces. They consumed the Azure Essence of the Sun’s Nourishment and drank the Empty Azure Mysterious Spirit. From then on, they roamed daily with the Five Thearchs and the Sun Lords. This is called the Way of Chasing the Sun.

*The Scripture of the Seventy-Four Transformations of the Supreme Clarity* states: If one can refine contemplation in a quiet chamber, cast aside worldly burdens, and sincerely focus on the vision of the Great Radiance, gazing upon the palaces of the Supreme Clarity, stabilizing qi through settled stillness, and calming the spirit within the Great Void, then within ten days one will behold the spirits, and within a year one will soar aloft. Accumulated resonance stirs within an inch, and transformations flourish upon the peaks of the clouds. One surveys the limits of the hundred spheres and masters the seventy-four wondrous transformations of the Dao. Blessings are immeasurable—these are the noble practices of the divine scriptures and the supreme esoteric formulas of the highest immortals.

It also says: If one can pacify the heart in the chamber, contemplate the divine countenance in its natural state, refine qi to reach the clear heavens, and let virtue flow through the nine fordings, then one will summon the hidden splendor of the numinous radiance, reviving the decayed and aged to endure forever. Blessings and felicity cling to the mysterious enterprise, and primordial auspiciousness disperses among one’s kin. This may be called enjoying the prosperity of life and death, while ancestors are reborn as embryonic immortals. Such is the wondrous transformation of the Great Image—how majestic is this numinous scripture!

*The Scripture of Natural Esoterica* says:
Close the eyes and visualize the Perfect Real,
Refine contemplation to summon the Ten Elders.
Ascend as an immortal, forever without action,
The divine countenance eternally wondrous and fair.
Thirst is quenched with the nectar of the Jade Pool,
Hunger is sated with the Golden Radiance Herb.

Thus, Master Chen, in cultivating the Dao and meeting the Perfected, necessarily took refined contemplation as the foundation and entering visualization through stillness as the priority.

**The Rites of Prolonged Fasting**
*The Great Mystery Scripture, Eighth Scroll: Commentary on the Transmission of Precepts by Laozi* states: In fasting and offerings, abundance or frugality should be arranged according to the occasion. The great method values clarity and emptiness, with simplicity as the highest principle.

*The Hidden Instructions on Ascending to Perfection, Fourth Scroll* says: Formerly, Ji Wei observed prolonged fasting for three years, exhausting his sincerity in solitary contemplation. Thereby, he was able to ingest the essence of the sun and moon’s radiance, and his body became suffused with divine light.

*The Declarations of the Perfected, Fifth Scroll* states: On days of *jiayin* and *gengshen*, when corpse-demons vie to disrupt the spirit and stir defilement, one must not share a mat with a spouse or engage in conversation. Instead, one should enter seclusion, fast, face east, and bow with the heart, visualizing the spirit and contemplating qi, awaiting the response of the divine luminaries. This accords with one’s intent in making offerings. By doing so, Jade Maidens will descend to attend.

For those who study the Dao, one must first restrain the hun and po souls, eliminate corpse-demons, and on the last day of the lunar month, the first day of the new moon, *gengshen* and *jiayin* days, enter seclusion, fast, bathe to cleanse the dust, and sit upright on a mat. It is best not to sleep. With a cinnabar brush, mark the left eye beneath the cheekbone, and with a realgar brush, mark the right side beneath the nose, allowing a small portion to enter the valley within. After marking, first knock the teeth together three times and silently pray:
*"The flying wrappings of the Upper Radiance scatter cinnabar and realgar as mist. Qi seizes the numinous and evil, corpse-defilement sinks and vanishes. Harmonize the hun and refine the po, unite the form with the Great Spirit. Grant me undying life, eternal preservation for ten thousand years, keen hearing and penetrating vision, perpetual advantage and smooth passage."*
After the prayer, knock the teeth together three more times, swallow saliva three times, and press the second finger of the right hand beneath the left eye seven times. Press firmly without lifting the hand. Then press these two points thoroughly—these are the gateways through which the seven po and wandering corpses travel, the bridges through which thieving spirits and evil qi pass. Thus, receiving the essence of cinnabar and realgar blocks the path of corpse-demons, while the two radiant forces fumigate and disperse chaotic qi. This is the supreme method of the Great Ultimate. By practicing it regularly, the hun and po become harmonious and gentle, corpse-defilement scatters and vanishes, and one attains the long life of the divine immortals, with penetrating vision and unimpeded qi. After three years of practice, lustful thoughts will entirely cease.

*The Scripture of Immeasurable [Virtue]* says: Observing prolonged fasting in the first month and reciting this scripture severs the earthly bonds of past lives’ wandering souls, delivering them to the Southern Palace. Observing prolonged fasting in the seventh month and reciting this scripture grants one the attainment of divine immortality, with one’s name inscribed in the Yellow Register of the heavens, erasing death and ascending to life. On the eight nodal days, reciting this scripture makes one a Perfected of the Nine Palaces. On one’s natal day, reciting this scripture purifies the hun-soul and spirit, preserves the myriad qi forever, spares one from suffering and distress, and grants a luminous body. The Three Realms will attend and guard, the Five Thearchs will receive, the myriad spirits will pay homage, one’s name will be recorded in the heavens, and upon the fulfillment of merit and virtue, one will ascend to the Supreme Clarity.

*The Declarations of the Perfected, Eighth Scroll* states: Xin Xuanzi, styled Yanqi, was a native of Dinggu in Longxi and lived during the reign of Emperor Ming of the Han. From youth, he was fond of the Dao, followed the precepts and commandments, cultivated苦行 with utmost sincerity, ate vegetables at midday, refined his form and preserved his essence, avoiding external distractions. Sometimes he wandered in the mountains and forests, shunning worldly dust. His aspiration was to rely on Master Jin of Mount Goushen and accompany Lingyang in treading the mysterious. Thus, he changed his name to Xuanzi and styled himself Yanqi. This is also recorded in *The Fourth Scroll of the Transmission of Daoist Learning*.

*The Scripture of the Lesser Kalpa* says: In burning incense and paying homage, one should eat once at midday.

*The Fourth Scroll of the Transmission of Daoist Learning* also states: Fan Chai was a native of Langzhong in Baxi. Fair-skinned with beautiful hair, fine eyebrows, and bright eyes, his demeanor was refined and elegant. He spoke only after being seen, never discussed omens or portents, was tranquil and desireless, and remained silent all day. He knotted tattered cloth into a net, wore straw to barely cover his body, went barefoot in winter and summer without his feet cracking, and never slept through the four seasons. In the fourteenth year of the Taiyuan era, he arrived in Jingzhou and resided at the tail of Fucheng Isle in Zhijiang County of Nan Commandery. There was a hut that did not shield against wind or frost. He used mulberry branches for a bed, with eastern straw stuffed between them. He had one empty bamboo container, one clay jar, and used a broken jar as a pillow to lean on while sleeping. Sometimes, he would carry the jar to beg for food for ten days. He abstained from polished rice, fine grains, rich wines, and flavorful fruits, consuming only coarse millet rice, vegetable broth, and about one *sheng* of food, which sufficed for over ten days.

Volume Ten states: Dongxiang Chaozong, styled Yilun, was a native of Qianzou in Gaomi. From childhood, he departed from worldly ways, avoiding marriage and officialdom. His conduct was earnest and sincere, enduring what others could not. He ate only at midday, his meal consisting solely of hemp and wheat. His disciples and family all admired his vegetarian fare, and in the refined hut where he dwelled, no fish or meat entered. Residing at the Hall of Rare Mystery, when Emperor Wu of Liang promoted the three teachings in unison, he decreed that all meals be vegetarian. Though edicts were issued, few could adhere to them. Yilun, however, observed the rule faithfully, so that all within the hall followed a vegetarian diet. If any privately violated the precept, they were immediately expelled. Even the kitchen offerings were bloodless, and far and near, people marveled at his purity and simplicity.

It further states: Fang Qianzhi, styled Daochong, was a native of Baixian in Zhaojun of Jizhou. He devoted himself to aiding others while neglecting his own body, observing the six periods of the day in fasting. During each of these six periods, he performed repentance rites for the ten directions. Few in the world could follow his example, so he often practiced alone. As his life neared its end, he suspended his fast for seven days before passing.

It further states: Zhang Min, styled Gaoming, was a native of Xuancheng. He dismissed his wife and children, left home to receive the Dao, and maintained a vegetarian diet in perpetual fasting. He regarded his seven-foot body as illusory, sparing no effort to cherish it. Secluding himself in the tranquility of Mount Wu, he cut off all desires for over twenty days. Fierce men and wild beasts gathered near his dwelling, and as his qi and life waned, his kin and friends urgently entreated him to eat. He reluctantly consented, and soon recovered. In the first year of the Dajian era of Chen, he again abstained from food and drink, saying, "I shall preserve this body, but it is not meant for long endurance. It benefits no one. Why strive for prolonged existence? To cultivate the Dao and establish conduct, must one remain here?" When others sought to persuade him further, he refused to listen.

Volume Eighteen states: Shen Faxi, styled Shizhen, was a native of Wukang in Wuxing and dwelled on Mount Zuo’e. Great propagators of the Dao would gather Daoists and laypeople on the fifteenth day of the first month to establish a communal fast and circumambulate the mountain with lanterns.

The *Precepts of the Supreme Clarity Great Cavern in Ninety-Two Articles* states: In practicing the Way of Feminine Unity, one may eat lightly at dawn but should not become full. At midday, one may eat a full meal, and after that, only sweet fruits and nuts are permitted.

The *Essentials of Ritual and Discipline for the Numinous Treasure Fast* states: Daoists observe perpetual fasting. After midday, only clear water may be drunk, and one may abstain from food entirely. At dawn, one drinks congee; at midday, one eats vegetables.

The *Baopuzi* states: Hong believed that those who observe extended fasts are either nobles or Daoists whose bodies are inherently weak and unable to endure the six periods of daily rites. He suggested burning incense and performing prostrations thrice by day, omitting the night. If one wishes to fast for a day and night, one may practice the six periods of the Dao. If one wishes to recite scriptures and lecture for a day, one may do so in three periods, with two periods at night for reviewing or reciting scriptures.

The *Upper Scroll of the Supreme Perfection Precepts* states: To delight in life, love the Dao, and cultivate its arts; to maintain a vegetarian diet in perpetual fasting until attaining the Dao—this is the foremost practice. Next are fasts of a thousand days, a hundred days, or a month; moderating and simplifying one’s diet; practicing qi refinement and taking medicinal herbs; and consuming sweet foods as one is able, while discreetly engaging in other matters. Urgent public or private affairs may temporarily interrupt these practices, but once resolved, one should resume without slackening body or mind. Thus may one become a perfected immortal. Those who practice in name only, with negligence and indolence, will face increased trials.

The precepts further state: In a year, the six months of the first, third, fifth, seventh, ninth, and eleventh lunar months are for fasting. Within a month, the first, eighth, fourteenth, fifteenth, eighteenth, twenty-third, twenty-fourth, twenty-eighth, twenty-ninth, and thirtieth days—these ten days are called the Ten Straight Fasts. On these days, celestial spirits descend, and those who cultivate diligently will gain blessings.

The *Lower Scroll of the Supreme Perfection Precepts* states: Perpetual fasting with the six periods may be practiced according to one’s capacity. For major rituals, constant recitation of scriptures, and lectures on auspicious days, communal fasts may be held in three periods to deliver the deceased, rescue the critically ill, absolve sins, and dispel misfortune—all may be practiced in six periods. For scripture recitation and lectures in three periods, two periods at night may be used for review or recitation.

It further states: Those who serve as teachers of the Dao and lead others in cultivation must have a fixed abode and proper attire, their movements and actions worthy of observation, their conduct exemplary. Thus do sages embrace the One as a model for the world, guiding transformation and guarding unity so that all under heaven return to the same source. Returning to purity and emptiness, guarding stillness with sincerity—though one may not yet be free from dependence, one should constantly learn to reduce selfishness, gradually relinquishing worldly affairs, and cultivate the Three Practices. In cultivating the Three Practices, fasting is fundamental. Fasting means alignment, purity, and stillness. It is not necessary to practice the six periods of the Dao, recite scriptures in three periods, or maintain nocturnal contemplation of spirits, repentance, and invocation of the divine. To lose even one of these is to forfeit the others. He who attains one must first master the three: he who masters the body sits upright and undisturbed; he who masters speech silently comprehends the profound; he who masters the mind unites spirit with the Dao. Such a one becomes a master and attains sagehood and immortality. Those who have not fully achieved this should master the body by performing morning rites and abstaining from killing, theft, and lust; master speech by reciting scriptures and refraining from falsehood, frivolous speech, divisive words, and abusive language; and master the mind by contemplating the spirit, relinquishing greed, anger, and delusion. Once the ten evils are cast aside, the ten virtues naturally arise, and one unites with the Dao in truth. Those who cannot do this should not presume to be teachers, nor forcibly establish governance for the sake of profit.

The *Lower Scroll of the Red Writ and Jade Instructions* states: In the Supreme Mystery Palace of the Northern Emperor, on Gengshen days, the Three Corpses and the spirits of the hun-souls report human transgressions to the Celestial Lord. On such days, if one observes fasting and upholds the precepts, contemplating the spirit day and night, the Three Corpses cannot ascend to heaven and accuse one of sins. The earthly officials report one’s good deeds, presenting them to the Celestial Lord. The Great Unity rejoices and records one’s name on the left contract, ensuring one’s place among the eternal people.

The Most High Supreme Palace’s Perfected and Divine Honored One regularly dispatches the Great Unity’s Central Terrace Envoy on Jiazi days to traverse all heavens and earths, inspecting the gods and spirits, dispersing miscellaneous vulgar ghosts and essences. If on such days one observes fasting and burns incense, the Central Terrace Envoy records all good deeds and memorializes them to the Three Heavens’ Supreme Emperor. The Supreme Emperor then removes one from the oversight of the celestial and terrestrial ghost-spirit overseers, inscribes one’s name in the Jade Register, and ensures one’s place as a Perfected Person forever.

The *Dharma Wheel Sutra* states: One maintains long fasts in secluded mounds, unwavering through day and night, partaking only of cypress and pine, drinking from limpid pools. One rests in shadowy caves, journeys alone, herds with deer, shelters the body in forests, sits among wild beasts, listens to the mournful cries of birds. Wind and clouds grow desolate, all things sink into eternal decay. Ice seals the ravines, pristine snow blankets the courtyard. The cold pierces the flesh, yet the will remains resolute. One endures hardship in the mountains, facing every trial without weariness, never seeking rest, ceaselessly seeking the Dao, until at last the imperial heart is moved.

The *Second Scroll of the Transmission of Daoist Learning* records: Celestial Master Zhang abandoned his home to study the Dao, carrying scriptures as he traveled. He entered the stone chamber of Mount Songgao, secluding himself for nine years of fasting. He wandered the Five Peaks, his concentrated devotion accumulating until the Perfected descended and the Dao was achieved. Thus he was called the Celestial Master.

The long fast is greatly emphasized in the various scriptures, but this is not elaborated here. Here ends the fifth scroll of the *Three Caverns’ Pearl Bag*.

**Sixth Scroll of the Three Caverns’ Pearl Bag**
*Compiled by the Tang Dynasty’s Master of the Vast Sea of Dao, Wang Xuanhe*

**On the Rites of Fasting Assemblies**

The *Eighth Scroll of the Supreme Mystery Canon: Commentary on the Transmission of Laozi’s Scriptures and Precepts* states: When transmitting the Dao and virtue in a fasting assembly, the ritual limit is thirty-eight persons; no fewer than six may be reduced. Of these six, one serves as the officiating master, and five as guarantors. The guarantors (*bao*) embody six meanings: treasure (*bao*), burden (*he*), illumination (*ming*), witness (*zheng*), deliverance (*du*), and completion (*cheng*). They are as precious as treasure, bearing the task of instruction; they illuminate sincere devotion, attest to virtuous practice, deliver through trials, and perfect the attainment of the utmost truth.

The fasting rites last nine, seven, five, or three days—no fewer than one. To reduce by even a single day renders it a gathering, not a fast. Distributing wealth to feed the worthy is called a gathering. Written petitions are submitted to invite overseers of the assembly. Thus, the *Laws of the Three Assemblies of the Mystic Capital* states: On the eighth day of the fourth month, celestial disciples assemble, all partaking in expiatory meals. The commentary explains: This releases celestial disciples from the wind-destroyed minor atonements for the sins of mortals.

Among the thirty-eight participants:
1. **Three Masters**: One principal master and two assisting masters—these are the Dharma Masters.
2. **Five Guarantors**: Five persons—these are the Chief Lecturers.
3. **Six Illuminators**: Six persons—these are the Fasting Overseers.
4. **Seven Witnesses**: Seven persons—these are the Scripture Attendants.
5. **Eight Deliverers**: Eight persons—these are the Incense Attendants.
6. **Nine Completers**: Nine persons—these are the Lamp Attendants.

If the full thirty-eight cannot be assembled, the number may vary according to circumstances. All must be disciples of divine attainment, persons of refined talent, capable of serving as guarantors and witnesses. Together, they receive the ritual texts and undertake the fast before the precepts are conferred.

The *Central Scroll of the Three Primordials Canon* states: On the fifteenth day of the first month (Celestial Official), the fifteenth day of the seventh month (Earthly Official), and the fifteenth day of the tenth month (Water Official), these three officials ascend to assemble at Jade Capital Mountain to review the ledgers of life and death, sin and fortune. On these days, fasting assemblies must be held.

**On the Relinquishment of Precepts**

The *Lower Scroll of the Perfected Regulations* states: If one who has received Daoist scriptures, precepts, or registers later finds cause to relinquish them, this is permitted, but one must not abandon them in betrayal. To depart without notice makes return difficult. If one relinquishes and later seeks to return, the path back to the supreme Dao remains open. Those who must depart should sincerely inform their master, who will offer parables and admonitions, establishing proper measures. If the measures are not established and the admonitions go unheeded, they shall burn incense, invoke the Three Treasures, and perform the Three Bows. With heart and mouth, they shall declare: “The scriptures, precepts, and regulations I have received are void with my person; the Three Realms, Six Destinies, and the Great Dao are all void; all dharmas are void, all is void.” After reciting this thrice and performing the Three Bows, they may depart, free to follow their wishes. However, they must never slander the true Dharma or reveal secret teachings. Violators shall forever fall into hell, with no hope of rebirth in goodness. Should one later regret and seek to re-receive the precepts, they must first establish merit, offering service and wealth, before regaining them according to the proper rites.

The *Lower Scroll of the Perfected Regulations* further states: If one’s precepts or registers are suddenly lost, half the penalty shall be remitted, and they need not re-receive them.

The *Lower Scroll of the Orthodox Unity Dharma Texts* states: For lost registers, the penalty is five bundles of firewood, three *liang* of cinnabar, and feeding three worthy persons. For the loss of one general register, the penalty is half a bundle of firewood, four *liang* of cinnabar, and feeding five worthy persons. For ten lost, one bundle of firewood, five *liang* of cinnabar, and feeding ten worthy persons. For seventy-five lost, ten bundles of firewood, seven *liang* of cinnabar, and feeding fifty worthy persons. For one hundred fifty lost, thirty bundles of firewood, nine *liang* of cinnabar, and feeding one hundred worthy persons. Once the penalty is fulfilled, the registers may be re-received.

It also states: If the loss is unintentional—whether at home or elsewhere, due to public or private coercion, fire, flood, theft, or banditry—one must truthfully report the time and place of the loss. If the lost register cannot be found, one shall atone by offering firewood and kitchen provisions to redeem the sin, then re-receive the registers, no longer bound by the original terms.

**On the Pure Precepts**

The *Eighth Scroll of the Supreme Mystery Canon: Commentary on the Transmission of Laozi’s Scriptures and Precepts* states: After receiving precepts or completing scripture study, one must fast on the last day of the lunar month and the fifteenth day. During the fast, one observes the Pure Precepts and the Gentle Precepts, reciting them a hundred or a thousand times through the night, without limit beyond the required number. Those capable of this may not reduce it below nine recitations. On other days of fasting or quietude, one may recite while walking, coming, or going, without waiting for the fast. Consult masters and fellow practitioners, reflecting and acting accordingly. One need not recite aloud; heart and mouth must align. In crowds, do not speak the words aloud; ensure they reside in the heart, and the perfected sages above will respond.

The *Lower Scroll of the Orthodox Unity Dharma Texts* states: All Daoist disciples shall first receive the protective talismans and the Three Precepts, then progress to the Five Precepts and Eight Precepts, before receiving registers. If one has not received precepts before receiving registers, they shall receive them afterward in proper sequence. Study and recitation must be fluent, with constant reflection and practice. Forgetfulness or error constitutes a violation. Before receiving registers, no spirits may be summoned; afterward, spirits respond to one’s every movement. Those who fail to uphold the precepts will find spirits unresponsive; transgressors will be forsaken by their divine attendants, who return to the celestial bureaus. The reviewing officials shall then impose calamities, illnesses, public and private disasters, misfortune, and failure in all endeavors. To achieve success, establish virtue, leave darkness for light, dispel evil with goodness, and replace misfortune with fortune—all depends on upholding the precepts. The spirits shall then protect them.

The precepts have distinct texts that must be studied and practiced with precision. Should one fail to comprehend, forget, or misinterpret them—or transgress due to coercion by superiors, fear of death, or deliberate violation—all such acts constitute offenses, collectively termed "breaking the precepts." One must then repent, confess, and reform. Those who violate the precepts bear false witness, betray the Dao to follow heterodoxy, and mingle with Buddhist and secular affairs. Such lack of devotion, divided loyalty, and wavering faith obstruct progress. If, after three admonitions from a master, one still fails to reform, it is deemed obstinacy; persistence in error is rebellion against the Dao. Defiance of the master’s authority warrants the revocation of one’s registers. Those who turn to Buddhism or secular pursuits, or abandon their master’s compassion, may seek redemption without reproach if they reform. Those who provoke others, forsake fundamentals for trivialities, or nominally follow the Dao while violating its true statutes shall find no refuge among the celestial bureaus. Only through prolonged repentance, renewed merit, and supplication may one regain favor and ascend through virtue. There is also *The Rites of Pure Precepts, Registers, and Offerings*, a separate volume for practice.

**On Merit, Prohibitions, and Taboos**
*The Green Statutes of the Central Palace of the Great Mysterious Capital* states: Those who cultivate the Supreme Clarity methods must not turn northward or face their natal direction, lest they offend the Jade Dawn and profane their original true nature. Five such violations bar one from immortality; ten incur punishment by the Left Bureau, leading to death and descent into the Three Paths of Hell, from which one may not reenter the human realm for ten thousand kalpas.

It further states: Disciples who receive the true methods of the Three Heavens and the Four Luminances, bearing the sacred writs and moving under the Three Radiances, must not sleep with their heads uncovered, nor appear without headwear or clothing, lest they insult their body-spirits and disgrace the true writs, causing the divine spirits to depart and leaving only an empty corpse. Three such violations bar one from immortality; five lead to death in hell, with no human rebirth for ten thousand kalpas.

It also states: Disciples who receive the true methods of the Three Heavens and the Four Poles’ Luminances must not recklessly enter defiled or mournful places, weep sorrowful tears, or offer condolences at funerals. Five such violations sever merit and obstruct immortality; ten lead to death in hell, with no human rebirth for ten thousand kalpas.

*The Yellow Plain Scripture of the Forty-Four Directions* states: Daoists practicing visualization of the supreme methods or cultivating the Great One must avoid seeing corpses or blood-impurities. They should dissolve a grain of cinnabar in water, then wash their eyes, rinse their mouth, and cleanse their hands and feet, reciting softly:
*"The Three Radiant Ways of the Upper Dao,
The Great One guards my form.
The Lord of Destiny, the Five Spirits of Yellow Peace,
Dispel blood-corpses, dissolve inauspicious impurities.
The Seven Axillae’ entanglements disperse,
The Five Viscera bloom anew.
Grant me transcendence,
Long to enjoy prosperity and integrity."*

Daoists receiving the methods of discipleship must not speak of death. Mentioning death disturbs the life-force, causing it to abandon its dwelling, allowing death-qi to enter. The soul departs, and malign qi lingers in the orifices, foreshadowing illness and death.

*The Scripture of the True One’s Regulations* states: Those who establish merit must not violate prohibitions or taboos. They should harmonize with their body-spirits, avoiding mutual harm. Such conflict invites disaster and misfortune. To dispel calamities, one must not act on their natal day or annual fate-day, as these harm the body.

On one’s natal day, one may circulate the Great Cycle of Heaven to refine qi and nurture the body, but must not act recklessly. On one’s annual fate-day, one may cultivate generative qi, nourish the spirit, and foster essence, but must not act recklessly. On the day of absolute fate, one must not act at all, lest it invite disaster and annihilation. On the day of Jupiter, one must not act, lest it invite official punishment and imprisonment. On the Six Harm days, one must not act, lest it invite illness, decline, and misfortune. On the last day of the lunar month, one must not act, lest it invite disaster, withering the body and dissipating qi. On the Year-Breaking day, one must not act, lest it invite disaster and familial misfortune.

The days of *wù-chén* and *wù-xū* are forbidden. *Xū* is the Celestial Gate, *chén* the Earthly Portal; *xū* is guarded by the Dog, *chén* by the Dragon. *Xū* is the Central King Spirit. On these days, the Venerable Elder visits the Most High Lord Lao to review and record the names of all men and women due for birth in the Jade Register. The Nine Elders visit the Nine Venerable Lords to review and record those due for death in the Death Register. The Virtue Elder visits the Lord of Virtue to record the merits of all men and women in the Left Contract. The Heavenly Emperor’s Elder visits the Heavenly Emperor to inscribe the transgressions of all men and women in the Right Contract. The Immortal Capital’s Elder visits the Lord of the Immortal Capital to record those destined for immortality in the Immortal Register. The Celestial Master returns to the Celestial Bureau to review the ledgers, distinguishing good from evil. On these days, the Celestial Gate is closed, the Earthly Portal sealed; dragons roam the Five Peaks, and dogs traverse the river bridges. The Central Yellow Dog Spirit guards the Celestial Gate, the Central Yellow Elder guards the Earthly Portal, and all external affairs are suspended. One must not burn incense, perform Daoist rites, or submit memorials.

Those who recklessly violate these days shall have their souls seized by the Central Yellow Great Spirit and delivered to the Prison of Inquiry for interrogation. For sixty days, no memorials may be submitted, and after sixty days of punishment, the souls shall be returned to their bodies, bringing misfortune, decline, loss, illness, and slander. If on *wù-xū* day one falls ill or faces official trouble, one should sit upright, reflect on transgressions, and repent sincerely. The deities shall perceive one’s sincerity and suspend punishment. If one submits a petition the following day, a decree of pardon shall be issued.

Moreover, it is said: Those who have received the Great One’s method and bear it within shall, upon encountering the mourning of parents, observe three months before the full term of mourning is complete; for *da gong* mourning, one month must pass. Only then may they perform Daoist rites and submit petitions or supplications.

Those who have received the Heavenly Perfected Three Ones or the Vermilion Realm of the True One’s method and bear it within shall, upon encountering the mourning of parents, observe one hundred days; for *qi* mourning, thirty days; for *da gong* mourning, one month. Before the monthly limit is fulfilled, they may not perform Daoist rites or submit petitions or supplications.

Those who bear the Yellow Writs and Contracts within shall, upon encountering the mourning of parents, observe one year; for *qi* mourning, one hundred days; for *da gong* mourning, forty days; for *xiao gong* mourning, one full month; for *si ma* mourning, one month. Before the monthly limit is fulfilled, they may not perform Daoist rites or submit petitions or announcements.

Should one violate these restrictions, they shall fall into the Prison of Level Yin. Within this prison, there is ever muddy mire, slippery and impassable; those under interrogation are forced to walk through the mire, unable to take a single step without falling to the ground. Thus shall they endure for three hundred years. Once the interrogation is complete, they shall be reborn as short, wretched beings, despised by all.

The *True Records, Ninth Scroll* states: On the *gēng-shēn* day of the first month, the *xīn-yǒu* day of the second month, the *gēng-xū* day of the third month, the *guǐ-hài* day of the fourth month, the *rén-zǐ* day of the fifth month, the *guǐ-chǒu* day of the sixth month, the *jiǎ-yín* day of the seventh month, the *yǐ-mǎo* day of the eighth month, the *jiǎ-chén* day of the ninth month, the *dīng-sì* day of the tenth month, the *bǐng-wǔ* day of the eleventh month, and the *dīng-wèi* day of the twelfth month—these are the days of the Supreme Thearch’s execution. On these days, no petitions may be made, and no affairs are auspicious.

The *Immortal Records of the Golden Writs* states: Those who study immortality...

Do not turn to face north when relieving yourself, nor look up at the Three Luminaries. Do not comb your hair, remove your clothes, or spit or curse while facing north—this violates the Destructive Decree of the Celestial Sovereign, which corresponds to the yearly *xià chén*. The "Sovereign" refers to the abode of the Sovereign *qi*. Do not curse the sun, moon, or stars. Do not impose punishments on the Eight Nodal Days. Do not harbor anger on the first day of the lunar month. Do not eat the hearts of a hundred herbs on the third day of the third month. Do not cut grass or fell trees on the eighth day of the fourth month. Do not draw blood on the fifth day of the fifth month. Do not break ground on the sixth day of the sixth month. Do not dwell on evil thoughts on the seventh day of the seventh month. Do not purchase footwear or items that touch the feet on the fourth day of the eighth month. Do not move bedding on the ninth day of the ninth month. Do not punish or reprimand others on the fifth day of the tenth month. Do not forgo bathing on the eleventh day of the eleventh month. Do not neglect fasting, burning incense, and reciting the names of immortals on the third day of the twelfth month. All such taboos are great prohibitions for heaven and humanity; the Three Officials record and examine them, deeming their violation a grave offense. Some cause the three *hun* and seven *po* to scatter and contend; others incur the hatred of the Womb Spirit, a time when the Three Officials receive evil. Thus, nightmares assail the cinnabar heart, malevolent spirits seize the vermilion gates, and at night, one offends the divine perfected. Afflictions flow and transform, and many prohibitions remain unknown to wondrous arts. If you can uphold and cultivate these precepts, you will become a candidate for immortality; if you violate the heavenly prohibitions, you will suffer harm and ruin.

The *Yellow Smoothness Scripture of Questions to the Supreme* states: Upon receiving the scriptures of Laozi, do not partake in vulgar sacrifices. It further states: Those who have received the Daoist methods should, when coming or going, avoid newly built or newly deceased households, and if they encounter a corpse or coffin on the road, upon returning to their dwelling, they must bathe with fragrant water before burning incense. It also states: Those who have received the methods must not enter the home of a woman in childbirth or see a corpse. If separated by distance or barriers, they may continue their daily rituals without restriction by day counts. If no such separation exists at home, they must wait forty-five days before resuming their rituals.

The *Lower Scroll of the Orthodox Unity Scriptures* states: To waver between the Dao and heterodoxy is to lack devotion; harboring dual intentions is foolish and indecisive, a betrayal of the Dao and a rebellion against one’s master and elders. The law decrees that such a person’s lifespan be shortened.

The *Supreme Yellow Simplicity Scripture of the Forty-Four Methods* states: In all matters of cultivating the Great One and practicing the supreme methods of spirit visualization, be cautious never to see a corpse or blood and filth. Seeing one corpse results in being unable to perform rituals for a year and forfeits a year’s progress. This is the discipline of the Imperial One, which retroactively penalizes past transgressions and blocks future advancement. If one sees three corpses in a year, the penalty is three years of forfeited progress and three years of suspended rituals. If one sees twenty-four corpses, they may never again cultivate the Great One in pursuit of immortality. It further states: For those who cultivate the supreme methods and the Way of the Feminine One and the Great One, the *qi* of the three *hun* and five spirits within the body constantly suffuses their headscarves and garments, while the essence of the seven *po* and nine numina dwells beneath their shoes. Thus, Daoist students must not sleep on shared mats, their hempen robes must not be lent to others, and their shoes must not be soiled by filth or touched by others, lest the three *hun* be startled. It also states: When cultivating the affairs of the Great One and making ritual vows, be cautious never to kowtow. Kowtowing overturns the Nine Heavens, disturbs the perfected, and causes the divine officials to reverse their decrees. The Mud Pill Palace is inverted, the Celestial Thearch wails in the Earthly Bureau, and the Great One weeps in the Central Field. Those who do this repeatedly gain no benefit from their visualization; the Three Perfected abandon their palaces, the Seven Spirits are buried and scattered, and the Dark Abode admits misfortune. This is the greatest taboo for the Five Spirits of the Great One. Therefore, those of true attainment merely visualize the act of kowtowing in their hearts, moving their essence to respond, without physically prostrating to invoke the numinous.

It further states: Those who cultivate the Way of the Great One and the Perfected must not perform ritual bows. Bowing is also taboo for the Five Spirits of the Imperial Lord. If one must make a vow during visualization, they should bow only in their heart, without physical prostration.

The *Upper Clarity Great Cavern Precepts of the Ninety-Two Articles* states: In practicing the Way of the Feminine One, one must not weep in sorrow. Weeping for even a moment causes the Five Spirits to wail in the Upper Bureau, the Great One to weep in the Central Field, the spirits to perish, the essence to vanish, and the numinous perfected to depart the body, leaving an empty corpse—what hope of immortality remains? It also states: One must not see a corpse; doing so results in being unable to perform rituals for a year and forfeits a year’s progress. If one sees three corpses in a year, they may not perform rituals for three years and forfeit three years’ progress. Seeing twenty-four corpses means losing the Dao; the earlier text of the *Supreme Simplicity* is largely in agreement with this. It further states: One must not speak of death or wish death upon oneself in anger. Speaking of death forty times disqualifies one from becoming a Perfected, as it is a sin of abandoning life, and within three years, the body will perish. It also states: One must not wear garments of the five colors. Adorning oneself in fine, ornate clothing causes the true spirits to depart, inner depravity to arise, the heart to run wild, the Three Corpses to flee in secret, the Red Child to take flight, and the Dark Chamber of the Long Separation to shatter the form and dissolve the bones, resulting in bodily death and the obliteration of one’s name. If one wears plain, undyed hempen robes, one may chant the Cavern Scriptures all day—what could one not attain? Riding clouds and driving dragons, one may roam the Great Ultimate.

The *Thirty-Six Precepts of the Numinous Treasure’s Inner Discipline for Immortals* states: Those who practice the dark arts should wear plain clothes and straw sandals; donning ornate garments results in losing the Dao. It also states: One must not speak of vulgar, heterodox, or filthy matters; three violations result in losing the Dao. It further states: One may bow to one’s paternal grandparents and parents if they follow the same Dao, but not otherwise.

Those of the same Dao from uncles and younger brothers downward may not be bowed to either. Violations result in bodily death.

It further states: One may not attend the auspicious gatherings of one’s parents.
It also states: Though parents, brothers, wives, and children share the same bond, and though they possess the merit of shared blood, none may sit on the same bed, eat from the same plate, for their Dao differs. All are considered corpse-defilement. Violations result in losing the Dao.

It further states: Husband and wife may not sleep in the same chamber, for impure thoughts arise in the heart, and the Dao is forever lost.
It also states: Unless bound by the same covenant, none may sleep in the same chamber; unless sharing the same bond, none may sit on the same bed, eat from the same plate, or wear the same clothes.

The *Numinous Treasure’s Regulations on Mourning Attire* states: During the year-long mourning for paternal grandparents, one may not approach the corpse but must observe mourning in a separate chamber. For five days, one may not receive condolences. The same applies to uncles and brothers, with a nine-month mourning period.
It further states: After the mourning rites are complete, one bathes, dons the headscarf and plain robes, and may not wear worldly attire. Violations result in losing the Dao, and the offense is severe, subject to the highest penalty. If one’s parents permit, one may extend mourning for a hundred days, then don the headscarf and coarse hempen robes, observing heart-mourning for three years without further outward grief—this is the *Numinous Treasure’s Audience Regulations*. If one retreats into the hidden mountains, all mourning and weeping are entirely severed.

The *Statutes on Establishing the Body and Practicing the Dao, Fifteenth* states: Those who bear the registers of immortal offices and numinous talismans may not bow or wail indiscriminately.
It further states: Before parents, the sovereign, officials of two thousand *shi*, provincial governors, and the Three Dukes, one must show reverence but may not perform ritual bows.

The *Statutes on Entering Governance, Twentieth* states: One may not enter governance within a month of a funeral; one may not enter governance if weeping exceeds three days; one may not enter governance if defiled by impurity before the new moon; one may not enter governance if three years have not yet passed a hundred days. All these refer to offenses of grief and defilement, for one dares not offend the divine luminaries. On *wu-chen* and *wu-xu* days, one may not enter governance; on days of taboo, one may not enter governance; when summoning officials or soldiers, on *bing-yin*, *ding-mao*, *bing-shen*, *ding-you*, *wu-shen*, and *wu-xu* days, one may not enter governance. Violations of taboos while practicing the Dao and cultivating truth result in the deduction of life-years. *Po* days may be used to dispel disasters, *Jian* days to establish merit, but days of punishment and harm may not be used. The annotation states: One may not use days of self-punishment, killing, or harm. When submitting memorials, one may not use *Jian*, *Po*, or *Bi* days.

The *Statutes on Submitting Memorials, Thirteenth* states: *Yin* punishes *Si*, *Xu* punishes *Wei*, *Zi* punishes *Mao*, *Shen* punishes *Yin*, *Mao* punishes *Zi*, *Si* punishes *Shen*, *Chou* punishes *Xu*, *Wei* punishes *Chou*.

The *Twentieth Statute* further states: One may not hold fasts or offer wine and meat within the *zhi*, for eating and drinking defile the primordial purity, incurring a penalty of forty-five days of plain fasting. The annotation states: Minor defilement lasts three days, major defilement seven days; one may seek absolution accordingly.

According to the *Three Caverns’ Regulations on Establishing Jing Halls, Eleventh*: A layperson’s hall is called *jing*; a master’s hall is called *zhi*. The statutes further cite: The *jing* must be established in the *Celestial Virtue*. *Celestial Virtue* refers to the earth of *jia*, *yi*, *bing*, and *ding*. It must be eighteen feet in length and sixteen feet in width. All who bear immortal talismans and registers must establish a *jing* or *zhi*.

The *Twentieth Statute* further states: One may not violate the taboos of the Three Masters or the four generations of the Three Masters’ ancestors. Violations incur a penalty of seven deductions from one’s life-span. These taboos also apply when entering the *zhi*. The annotation states: The Celestial Master is one’s lineage master; the taboos include the names of the master’s great-grandfather, grandfather, father, and the master himself.

*Precepts of the Eight Prohibitions for Fasting, Presented with Full Titles by Your Servant Lu Xiujing*:

The Primordial Celestial Worthy, the Boundless Great Dao, the Responsive and Numinous Sage, and all divine luminaries—now there are good men and good women who seek to receive and uphold the Eight Precepts, observing a pure fast for one day and one night, using it to restrain body and mind and extinguish the afflictions of the three karmic actions.

The *Cavern Spirit Scripture, Twelfth* states: Fasting is urgent for alignment, for aligning body and mind. When body and mind are aligned, one remains free from disorder and decay. Decay arises from many causes, but the major ones are eight:
1. One may not kill living beings to sustain oneself;
2. One may not indulge in lust for pleasure;
3. One may not steal from others to provide for oneself;
4. One may not lie to demonstrate ability;
5. One may not become intoxicated to indulge the will;
6. One may not recline on high, broad, and grand beds;
7. One may not compete in adorning oneself with fragrant oils;
8. One may not indulge in song and dance to perform as an entertainer.

If today’s good men and good women can refrain from these eight transgressions, the eight forms of decay will have no means to arise, and the Eight Precepts will naturally be established. If upheld without lapse for a long time, one will prolong life and preserve destiny, attaining divine penetration and unobstructed insight. Therefore, those who fast receive and uphold the Eight Precepts, contemplate the truth, and practice the Dao, will find their path boundless and their manifestations swift, all as expected. Now that the reception is complete, one bows twice, rises twice, and retires while upholding the precepts.

*Three Caverns Pearl Satchel, Scroll Six* concludes.
*Three Caverns Pearl Satchel, Scroll Seven* begins.

The Venerable Wang Xuanhe of Luhai, Feathered Guest of the Great Tang, on the *Twenty-Four Treatises*
—Following *The Mysterious Capital Precepts, Scroll Sixteen*:

A "treatise" (治) pertains to the abode of one’s nature, life, soul, and spirit.

*The Chart of the Five Marchmounts and Famous Mountains* states:
The **Yangping Treatise** belongs to Metal and the Horn Star.
The **Lutang Treatise**, Metal and the Neck Star.
The **Heming Treatise**, Wood and the Root Star.
The **Liyuan Treatise**, Earth and the Chamber Star.
The **Ge Gui Treatise**, Fire and the Heart Star.
The **Gengchu Treatise**, Fire and the Tail Star.
The **Qinzhong Treatise**, Water and the Winnowing Basket Star.
The **Zhenduo Treatise**, Metal and the Dipper Star.
These eight treatises are the **Upper Treatises**.

The **Changli Treatise**, Earth and the Ox Star.
The **Lishang Treatise**, Fire and the Woman Star.
The **Yongquan Treatise**, Wood and the Void Star.
The **Chougeng Treatise**, Fire and the Rooftop Star.
The **Beiping Treatise**, Metal and the House Star.
The **Benzhu Treatise**, Wood and the Wall Star.
The **Mengqin Treatise**, Fire and the Straddling Star.
The **Pinggai Treatise**, Earth and the Bond Star.
These eight treatises are the **Middle Treatises**.

The **Yuntai Treatise**, Fire and the Stomach Star.
The **Jinkou Treatise**, Wood and the Pleiades Star.
The **Houcheng Treatise**, Earth and the Net Star.
The **Gongmu Treatise**, Metal and the Beak Star.
The **Pinggang Treatise**, Water and the Orion Star.
The **Zhubu Treatise**, Metal and the Well Star.
The **Yuju Treatise**, Water and the Ghost Star.
The **Beimang Treatise**, Earth and the Willow Star.
These eight treatises are the **Lower Treatises**.

The above twenty-four treatises were all established by the Most High Lord Lao in the first year of *Han’an* during the Later Han. The **Ganghu Treatise** belongs to Water and the Star Star. The **Baishi Treatise**, Metal and the Spread Star. The **Zhongmao Treatise**, Water and the Wings Star. The **Jushan Treatise**, Earth and the Chariot Star. *The Terrestrial Map* states: These four treatises lie northeast of the capital. These four were added by Celestial Master Zhang to complete the twenty-four treatises, forming twenty-eight treatises in total, corresponding to the twenty-eight lunar lodges.

The **Pinggong Treatise**, belonging to Water, pairs with the **Yongquan Treatise**.
The **Gongmu Treatise**, belonging to Earth, pairs with the **Chougeng Treatise**.
The **Tiantai Treatise**, belonging to Earth, pairs with the **Benzhu Treatise**.
The **Laixiang Treatise**, belonging to Metal, pairs with the **Changli Treatise**.
The **Zunling Treatise**, belonging to Metal, pairs with the **Yuntai Treatise**.
The **Daiyuan Treatise**, belonging to Metal, pairs with the **Yuntai Treatise**.
The **Lili Treatise**, belonging to Fire, pairs with the **Lishang Treatise**.
The **Liyuan Treatise**, belonging to Metal, pairs with the **Changli Treatise**.
These eight treatises were further added by the Celestial Master to match the eight ranks, spreading throughout the four seas to pacify the realm and transform its people.

**First: The Four Separate Treatises**
1. **Jushan Treatise**
2. **Zhongmao Treatise**
3. **Baishi Treatise**
4. **Ganghu Treatise**
These four ranks are called *Separate Treatises* externally and *Complete Treatises* internally. The Complete Treatises fulfill the twenty-eight, while the Separate ones diverge from the three eights.

**Second: The Eight Wandering Treatises**
1. **Jiyang Treatise**
2. **Pingdu Treatise**
3. **Hefeng Treatise**
4. **Cimu Treatise**
5. **Huangjin Treatise**
6. **Taihua Treatise**
7. **Qingcheng Treatise** (*The Jade Talisman Scripture* renders it as *Qingcheng Mountain*)
8. **Emei Treatise**
These eight ranks are the *Wandering Treatises*.

**Third: The Eight Paired Treatises**
1. **Daiyuan Treatise**
2. **Zunling Treatise**
3. **Laixiang Treatise**
4. **Tiantai Treatise**
5. **Gongmu Treatise**
6. **Pinggong Treatise**
7. **Lili Treatise**
8. **Liyuan Treatise**
These eight ranks are the *Paired Treatises*.

**Fourth: The Twenty-Four Proper Treatises**
1. **Beimang Treatise**
2. **Yuju Treatise**
3. **Zhubu Treatise**
4. **Pinggang Treatise**
5. **Gongmu Treatise**
6. **Houcheng Treatise**
7. **Jinkou Treatise**
8. **Yuntai Treatise**
These are the eight *Lower Treatises*.

1. **Pinggai Treatise**
2. **Mengqin Treatise**
3. **Benzhu Treatise**
4. **Chougeng Treatise**
5. **Beiping Treatise**
6. **Yongquan Treatise**
7. **Lishang Treatise**
8. **Changli Treatise**
These are the eight *Middle Treatises*.

1. **Zhenduo Treatise**
2. **Qinzhong Treatise**
3. **Gengchu Treatise**
4. **Ge Gui Treatise**
5. **Liyuan Treatise**
6. **Heming Treatise**
7. **Lutang Treatise**
8. **Yangping Treatise**
These are the eight *Upper Treatises*.

**Fifth: The Twenty-Eight Stellar Treatises**
The Upper Treatise is also called the *Inner Treatise*, the *Great Treatise*, or the *Proper Treatise*, established by the Supreme Mysterious Elder, the Most High Great Dao Lord, on the seventh day of the seventh month in the first year of *Shanghuang*.

**Essential Secrets of the Twenty-Eight Treatises, Upper, Middle, and Lower Ranks:**
1. **Horn Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Boundless, formless and void; the Lower Treatise is **Yangping Mountain**.
2. **Neck Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Boundless, naturally void; the Lower Treatise is **Lutang Mountain**.
3. **Root Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Mysterious Void, non-action; the Lower Treatise is **Heming Mountain**.
   These three treatises govern those born in the *chen* hour.

4. **Chamber Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Void White; the Lower Treatise is **Liyuan Mountain**.
5. **Heart Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Cavern White; the Lower Treatise is **Ge Gui Mountain**.
   This treatise governs those born in the *mao* hour.

6. **Tail Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Three Ones; the Lower Treatise is **Gengchu Mountain**.
7. **Winnowing Basket Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Three Origins; the Lower Treatise is **Qinzhong Mountain**.
   This treatise governs those born in the *yin* hour.

8. **Dipper Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Three Fives; the Lower Treatise is **Zhenduo Mountain**.
   This treatise governs those born in the *chou* hour.
   The above eight ranks have no Upper Treatise.

9. **Ox Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Nine Heavens; the Lower Treatise is **Changli Mountain**.
10. **Woman Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Five Cities; the Lower Treatise is **Lishang Mountain**.
    Combined with the previous three, these govern those born in the *chou* hour.

11. **Void Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Original Spirit; the Lower Treatise is **Yongquan Mountain**.
12. **Rooftop Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Cinnabar Field; the Lower Treatise is **Chougeng Mountain**.
    This treatise governs those born in the *zi* hour.

13. **House Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Constant Radiance; the Lower Treatise is **Beiping Mountain**.
14. **Wall Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Golden Beam; the Lower Treatise is **Benzhu Mountain**.

These two treatises govern those born in the *hai* hour.

15. **Straddler Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Six Palaces; the Lower Treatise is **Mengqin Mountain**.
16. **Harvester Star**: The Upper Treatise is the One Sovereign; the Lower Treatise is **Pinggai Mountain**.
    This treatise governs those born in the *xu* hour.

The middle eight ranks are governed by the Mysterious Elder.

17. **Stomach Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Five Dragons; the Lower Treatise is **Yuntai Mountain**.
    Combined with the previous three, these govern those born in the *xu* hour.
18. **Mao Star**: The Upper Treatise is Following Heaven; the Lower Treatise is **Jinkou Mountain**.
19. **Net Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Six Ding; the Lower Treatise is **Houcheng Mountain**.
    This treatise governs those born in the *you* hour.
20. **Turtle Beak Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Twelve; the Lower Treatise is **Gongmu Mountain**.
21. **Three Stars**: The Upper Treatise is Returning to the Body; the Lower Treatise is **Pinggang Mountain**.
    This treatise governs those born in the *shen* hour.
22. **Well Star**: The Upper Treatise is Restraining Spirits; the Lower Treatise is **Zhubu Mountain**.
23. **Ghost Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Formless; the Lower Treatise is **Yuju Mountain**.
    This is not a mountain.
24. **Willow Star**: The Upper Treatise is Gathering Primal Qi; the Lower Treatise is **Beimang Mountain**.
    These two treatises govern those born in the *wei* hour.

The lower eight ranks are governed by the Most High.

On the seventh day of the first month in the second year of *Han’an* of the Most High, at the hour of noon, the twenty-four treatises—upper eight, middle eight, and lower eight—were aligned with the twenty-four qi and bestowed upon Celestial Master Zhang Daoling.

25. **Star Mansion**: The Upper Treatise is Distinct Form; the Lower Treatise is **Ganghu Mountain**.
26. **Spread Star**: The Upper Treatise is Preserving Qi; the Lower Treatise is **Baishi Mountain**.
    This treatise governs those born in the *wu* hour.
27. **Wings Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Five Kings; the Lower Treatise is **Zhongmao Mountain**.
28. **Chariot Star**: The Upper Treatise is the Golden Hall; the Lower Treatise is **Jushan Mountain**.
    These two treatises govern those born in the *si* hour.

In the first year of *Jian’an*, on the seventh day of the first month, the Celestial Master revealed the lower four treatises, naming them the Complete Treatises. Together with the previous twenty-eight treatises, they fully correspond to the twenty-eight lunar lodges.

The stellar treatises are established in accordance with Heaven, and through the cycles of kalpas, those who receive the mandate as Celestial Masters each clarify and propagate the teachings to save the world and deliver humanity, until the era of Great Peace. When the Lord of Great Peace emerges, additional offices will be established, and those with talent and virtue will be promoted to the rank of Great Spirits.

Furthermore, the *Illustrated Twenty-Four Treatises of Celestial Master Zhang* states: On the seventh day of the first month in the second year of *Han’an* of the Most High, at the hour of noon, the twenty-four treatises—upper eight, middle eight, and lower eight—were aligned with the twenty-four qi of Heaven and the twenty-eight lunar lodges, and bestowed upon Celestial Master Zhang Daoling for propagation and transformation.

Celestial Master Zhang, a native of Feng County in Pei State, was named Daoling, styled Fuhan. His nature was stern and upright; he was learned in the classics and cultivated in conduct, mastering the Dao with skill. In the second year of *Yongping*, the Han Emperor issued an edict appointing him Prefect of Jiangzhou in Ba Commandery.

In the first year of *Yuanhe*, on the tenth day of the third month (a *xinchou* day), an imperial edict appointed him Minister of Works. The Duke was enfeoffed as Marquis of Jixian County, tasked with gathering *zhi* herbs and compiling illustrated classics of immortals to procure for the state elixirs of longevity and transcendence.

In the first year of *Han’an*, on a *dingchou* day, an edict summoned him to respond to the Most High. He then resigned his office and entered the territory of Yizhou. In that same year, within the boundaries of Linqiong County in Shu Commandery, at Red Stone City on Queting Mountain, he settled in tranquil contemplation. On the first day of the fifth month, at midnight, a procession of a thousand chariots and ten thousand riders descended before Red Stone City. Golden carriages and feathered canopies were accompanied by an innumerable host of dragon and tiger spirits, ghostly soldiers, and attendants. Five figures appeared among them:

One declared, “I am the Archivist Beneath the Pillars of Zhou.”
Another said, “I am the Most High Lord Lao, newly manifested.”
A third announced, “I am the Central Yellow Perfected Sovereign, the Most High August Emperor.”
A fourth stated, “I am Zhang Liang, Master of the Han.”
The fifth proclaimed, “I am the maternal grandfather of the Celestial Master, the Han’s aide, Master Ziyuan.”
