Xi again bowed and said: "I beseech you, Master, to compose a text for me, expounding the meaning of the Great Dao, that I may uphold and cultivate it." In the first year of *Wu Ji*, the *guichou* year, on the twenty-eighth day of the twelfth month at noon, Laozi composed the *Classic of the Dao and Virtue* in two scrolls and bestowed it upon Xi.

Laozi prepared to depart. Xi said: "May I follow you, Master, on your distant travels and witness the transformations of heaven and earth?" Laozi replied: "My path has no fixed abode—I may ascend to heaven, descend into the earth, scale mountains, or plunge into the sea. I may dwell in the lands of the Rong, Di, Man, and Mo, in realms beyond human reach, among spirits and demons, or in perilous straits. I observe the transformations of the ten directions, passing through all barriers, appearing and vanishing at will. You, having only just received the Dao, have not yet purified your impurities—how could you follow me on such a journey? Remain here and recite these two scrolls ten thousand times. When the Dao is perfected within you, then you may accompany me. When your cultivation nears completion, I shall come to receive you. For now, you may not depart."

As Laozi was about to leave, he instructed: "After a thousand days, seek me at the marketplace gate of Chengdu, at the stall of the green sheep." Xi reverently followed his teaching, reciting the scripture ten thousand times. After a thousand days, his body could fly, and he walked through fire and water without burning or drowning. Now that his Dao was perfected, he went to the marketplace gate of Chengdu, to the stall of the green sheep, to seek Laozi. After searching all day without success, he spent the night in longing. On the ninth day, he saw a man come to buy green sheep. Thereupon, he understood and asked the servant: "Why do you buy these green sheep every day?" The man replied: "My master has a distinguished guest who favors green sheep, so he sends me to purchase them." Xi said: "I once had an old acquaintance with that guest. We agreed to meet here—could you convey a message for me?"

Xi then presented precious treasures to him. The servant said: "Very well. You may follow me, and I shall fully convey this message." Xi said: "If so, tell the guest that Guanling Yin Xi awaits outside." The servant relayed his words as instructed. Laozi said: "Summon him forward." Brushing his robes, he rose and ascended his seat of natural lotus, then asked Xi: "Since we parted these three years, what gains and losses have you found in reciting the scripture?" Xi bowed and declared: "By following your teaching and reciting the scripture, I have attained perpetual life without death."

Laozi said: "You once wished to accompany me on distant travels—now that your Dao is perfected, we may journey beyond the eight limits of the great earth." Xi replied: "My long-held wish is at last fulfilled; I have no regrets remaining." Thereupon, Laozi ordered the carriage prepared, and they roamed far between heaven and earth, transforming through many lands. Later, they entered the hermitage of Mount Grdhrakūṭa in the kingdom of Yanbin. As the king of Yanbin was traveling abroad, he asked: "What manner of man is this?" His attendant replied: "A Daoist." The king said: "How does a Daoist come to dwell in seclusion here?"

The next day, upon seeing them again during his travels, the king asked: "What practice do you cultivate that may bring fortune?" Laozi said: "Through fasting, moderation in eating, reciting scriptures, and walking the Dao—above, one may attain the True and achieve deathlessness, transcending birth and death, with transformation and passage governed by intent; below, one may secure the state and prosper the household, or follow the turning of the body to attain the Dao, transcend the world, and enter non-action." The king said: "Excellent!" The following day, as he traveled forth, he saw them once more.

The king asked: "What is most valued in the Daoist arts?"

The Daoist replied: "Our Way prizes naturalness, purity, stillness, and non-action. Through fasting, moderation in eating, and burning incense, one may ascend to heaven, be born into the households of kings and marquises, or follow the Dao to transcend the world—this is the highest attainment."

The king said: "Excellent! I wish to invite the Daoists to partake in the midday meal and practice the Dao. Would that be permissible?"

The Daoist asked: "How many would you invite?"

The king said: "All of them."

The Daoist replied: "There are too many disciples to provide for."

The king laughed and said: "I rule a great kingdom—what could I not obtain? How could I be unable to provide?"

The Daoist said: "We Daoists are but poor followers of the Way, relying on the king’s support. Even the treasures we possess belong to the king. Now, I first wish to invite the people of the kingdom to partake in the midday meal, that we may pray for blessings on their behalf. Would that be acceptable?"

The king said: "Very well! Though I fear the Daoists lack the means to provide for them."

The Daoist replied: "We have sufficient provisions. I humbly request Your Majesty’s presence."

The king said: "I shall arrive on the appointed day."

The Daoist then first invited the ministers and the people of the kingdom, sending immortal youths and jade maidens, along with flying immortals from the four directions, to summon men and women for fourteen days. When all had gathered, the king sighed and said: "Even a poor Daoist can perform such great blessings—how could I, a great king, lack anything and claim inability to provide?"

On the appointed day, he invited the Daoist disciples to a grand assembly. As they arrived, they brought forth the nine ranks of celestial sages and immortals, with over forty days of arrivals unceasing. Later, each day brought strange and varied guests—some Hu, some Cang, some Wu, some Chu—some tall, some short. Half the king’s granaries and treasuries were depleted, yet the people kept coming.

The king said: "As the Daoist said, why are there so many? I truly fear exhaustion and lack of provisions, and suddenly a wicked thought arose: *I suspect this old man is a demonic spirit, not a worthy sage.* Bind the Daoist quickly, pile firewood in the marketplace, and burn him to death as a warning to the people."

Thereupon, they bound Laozi and his disciples. Laozi, unperturbed, allowed them to act, gathering firewood in the city square. He then said to Xi and the other perfected ones: "Simply follow me atop this pyre. Though the entire kingdom comes to watch, they will be unable to harm us."

When the people of the kingdom saw this, those of good heart all exclaimed in dismay: "Why does our king do this?"

The people pleaded desperately for the Daoist, yet he was burned midway—how pitiable, how lamentable! The flames soared to the heavens, and as the kingdom’s people watched, Laozi radiated a body of light that filled the world. Amid the smoke and embers, Laozi, Xi, and the perfected ones sat upon lotus blossoms, holding the *Dao De Jing* and chanting its verses. Even as the fire raged fiercely, they remained seated upon the coals, unmoving.

The king asked, “Is the old master dead yet?”
The messenger replied, “The old master still sits upon the embers, reciting the scripture.”

The king then ordered Laozi to be cast into the deep abyss. Yet when they followed him into the depths, he did not drown. The people saw Laozi emanating light, borne upon a divine dragon whose radiance also illuminated the abyss. There he continued his recitation, untouched by harm.

The king asked, “Are the Daoists dead now?”
The messenger said, “When cast into the deep abyss, the Dragon King emerged to bear him up. The old master’s light shone throughout the kingdom, and again he neither drowned nor died. What is to be done?”

The king said, “Burning him does not kill him, drowning him does not submerge him—what can I do?” Turning to his ministers, he asked, “Could that old master be a heavenly teacher, a sage? Now I wish to serve him—what say you?”

The ministers replied, “Excellent!”

Fearing the old master’s wrath would bring ruin to the kingdom, the king was advised to humble himself and offer apologies. The king replied, “Just so.” He personally approached Laozi and recounted the past events, prostrating himself in apology.

Laozi said, “Earlier, I warned you that you might be unable to provide for us, yet you turned and burned my disciples. How could you defy Heaven and act so lawlessly? Heaven does not permit your wanton slaughter of the innocent. It is because Heaven sees my innocence that I have passed through these perils unharmed. Heaven is about to destroy your kingdom—its fall will come soon.”

The king deeply apologized, admitting his guilt, and pledged to place the entire nation in service to the master, vowing never to grow negligent. Laozi said, “Though you now bow your head a thousand times, your past malice makes your sincerity uncertain. I fear you may yet regret this. What oath will you swear?”

The king replied, “From this day, I shall have all men and women of the kingdom remain unmarried for life, shaving their heads and beards as a covenant. If I break this vow, may I die as proof. How is this?”

Laozi said, “Good.” Then he appointed Yin Xi as the master and commanded the king and his people to serve him. The king was to entrust governance to his crown prince, Yili, while he himself would cultivate the Dao, abandoning his kingdom to seek liberation for the world.

Laozi said, “Excellent! If you wish to renounce your kingdom and study the Dao, I shall leave you a teacher, who shall be called *Fofo*, to serve the Supreme Perfect and True Way. The Dao possesses great methods: if you remain in your kingdom to cultivate, simply uphold the Five Precepts and the Ten Virtues, and you will attain blessings, dispel misfortune, perpetually dwell in the human realm, and enjoy honor, wealth, and nobility. Through this, you may also attain the Dao and liberate the world—why must you abandon your home?”

The king and his ministers all bowed their heads before the master, and on that same day, men and women alike took up the Dao. They were given the three monastic robes, instructed to guard and refine their minds, and given staffs to ward off snakes and insects. They observed moderation in alms-begging as discipline.

Laozi then composed ninety thousand volumes of scriptures and precepts, which they began reciting that very day. Laozi said, “Now that I have transmitted the Dao to you in full, I wish to swiftly journey to the eight directions.” He then returned to his eastern travels, where he expounded the primordial qi of the Great Dao in seclusion, establishing three teachings: the first was the *Supreme Boundless Great Dao*, the second was the *Supreme Perfect and True Way*, and the third was the *Great Peace and Austerity Way*.

The *Scripture of Laozi’s Conversion of the Barbarians* states: “During the reign of King You, I emerged as a teacher to instruct in the methods of the Dao. Observing the emptiness and fullness of the times, I served as the Archivist Under the Pillar, surnamed Li, named Er, styled Boyang. Knowing King You could no longer be guided, I resolved to depart, for this age of decline and chaos could not be endured. As King You of Zhou was about to lose his kingdom, I disguised myself, riding a black ox and a simple wooden cart, and left.” Thus, King You was indeed slain by the Great Rong.

Then he journeyed westward to the kingdom of Jibin, arriving at the Hangu Pass. The Pass Prefect Yin Xi was devoted to the arts of the Dao and inner cultivation, versed in celestial patterns above and terrestrial principles below. Foreseeing that the Dao would pass westward, he observed the heavens day and night. At that time, in the twelfth month of the *guichou* year, on the twenty-fifth day—the end of the La festival—the Dao indeed came, crossing the pass from the east. Prefect Yin Xi had previously instructed his gate officers: “Today, an old man riding a black ox and a simple wooden cart will come to cross the pass. When you see him, detain him and do not let him leave!”

As foretold, Laozi arrived at the pass riding a black ox and a plain wooden cart. The officers detained him, refusing passage. Laozi said: “I am but a poor old man living east of the pass, with fields to the west. Tomorrow is the La festival, and I wish to gather firewood. Pray, allow me to cross.” The officer knelt and replied: “The Prefect has ordered that if an old man riding a black ox and a simple wooden cart appears, he must be detained. I beg you to stay a moment.” The officer then entered to report to the Pass Prefect.

The Prefect, bearing his seal and tablet, came forth to welcome him and prepared a ritual reception. Laozi said: “I am but a poor old man living east of the pass, with fields to the west. Tomorrow is the La festival, and I wish to gather firewood. Why detain me?” Yin Xi knelt, holding his tablet, and said: “I am Yin Xi, a native of Chengdu in Shu Commandery. From birth until now, I have lived through three thousand *jiazi* cycles. I have sought you through hardship and exposure, and by heaven’s grace, we meet today. I beg you to stay a while.”

Laozi entered the lodge, and they spoke for three days and nights. Yin Xi prepared a lavish feast, and Laozi, feeling he had no way to repay such generosity, composed the *Five Thousand Character Text* in two scrolls—the *Upper* and *Lower Scriptures*—and bestowed them upon him in gratitude. Then he prepared to depart. Yin Xi said: “May I know your honorable name?” Laozi opened his mouth and stuck out his tongue, saying: “All my teeth have fallen out; only my tongue remains.” Yin Xi said: “Lao Dan’s teeth numbered thirty-six in his mouth, white as frost. Now they are all gone, and only the tongue remains. Thus I know that the soft can overcome the hard, and the weak can conquer the strong. I wish to cultivate the resolve of softness and weakness.” Laozi did not disclose his name and departed.

Yin Xi said: “I admire the beauty of the Dao and virtue; I wish to follow you westward.” Laozi replied: “I wander beyond the bounds of heaven and earth, dispersing my *qi* to the eight directions. Sometimes I visit small kingdoms, sometimes ascend to heaven or descend into the abyss, teaching and transforming wherever I go. How could you follow me?” Yin Xi knelt and said: “I would enter water or plunge into the abyss, ascend to heaven or descend into the earth, risking my life to follow you.” Laozi said: “Diligently study the *Five Thousand Character Text*—the *Upper* and *Lower Scriptures*. Three years hence, seek me at the Green Ram Market in Chengdu. You will find me there.” Yin Xi could not follow him then, and so, in the *guichou* year, they parted.

Yin Xi thereafter devoted himself to the scriptures, practicing day and night without rest. His primordial *qi* returned to his body, and each day his understanding of the Dao deepened, confirming its truth. Later, in the *dingsi* year, he traveled to the Green Ram Market in Chengdu to seek Laozi. Days and months passed without success, and he sighed in longing. Then he noticed a man who came daily to buy green rams. His heart opened in realization, and he asked: “Why do you come every day to buy these green rams?” The man replied: “My master has a distinguished guest who favors green rams, so he sends me to buy them.” Yin Xi said: “I once had an appointment with that guest here. Could you convey a message for me?” He offered precious treasures. The man said: “Very well. Follow me, and I will inform him.” Yin Xi said: “If so, tell your master that Yin Xi is outside.” The man relayed the message as instructed.

Laozi said: “Let him enter.” He brushed his robes, rose, and ascended a natural lotus throne, grasping a nine-jointed staff. Seeing Yin Xi, he said: “Why are you late? I have waited for you a long time.” Yin Xi bowed twice and said: “I have sought you for days and months, not knowing where you had gone. The Dao does not betray its promise. Now that I see you, your grace is as vast and deep as the heavens! How could I forget anything from these three years?” He prostrated himself and said: “Since parting from you, I have studied the scriptures you gave me day and night, memorizing them without fear of forgetting. Malevolent spirits and demonic thieves, seeing me, naturally submit. The myriad spirits flee before me. I have come to know the boundlessness of primordial *qi*.”

Laozi said: “I have waited for you a long time, knowing your unshakable resolve. I shall take you on a distant journey to observe the primordial *qi* between heaven and earth and preserve your bodily form. Is this not excellent?” Then, in the *dingsi* year, he took Yin Xi to the western lands, wishing to teach the people of those kingdoms without being recognized. Arriving in the kingdom of Jibin, they entered the mountains, dwelling in caves and practicing the Dao for three years.

In the *gengshen* year, the Hu king went hunting and repeatedly saw them. He asked his attendants: “What manner of men are these?” None could answer. Laozi replied: “I am an old man who has long dwelled in these mountains.” The king found this strange, suspecting them to be mountain spirits, unaware they were sages. He was determined to harm Laozi. Laozi, embodying the resolve of softness and weakness, humbled himself and prepared a feast of the *Supreme Boundless Celestial Kitchen*, inviting the people of the kingdom. The king, hearing this, clapped his hands and laughed: “This old man depends on our kingdom for his livelihood. How could he invite our people?” Laozi said: “I have relied on the king’s land to live until today. Now, as I prepare to return to the eastern lands, I wish to repay the king’s kindness. Let us set a date for the gathering.”

The king dispatched envoys to inspect the preparations for Laozi’s feast. Laozi had arranged tents woven from the qi of the Five Phases: white silk in the Western Valley, black silk in the Northern Valley, azure silk in the Eastern Valley, crimson silk in the Southern Valley, and yellow silk at the center. He invited the king himself, along with all the people of the kingdom. The Hu king then summoned thirty-six nations, numbering millions, to gather within Laozi’s five-colored cloud-silk tents. They feasted for seven days and seven nights, the banquet ever-abundant, without weariness or exhaustion.

Upon returning to his kingdom, the Hu king wished to invite Laozi again. Laozi replied to the king: “I cannot be invited.” The king said: “In my great kingdom, what is there that we lack? Why should I be unable to invite you?” He set a date for the gathering.

On the appointed day, Laozi arrived with his fellow Daoists. Four groups of disciples attended him, along with the Four Heavenly Kings and a million followers—each day, one kind of person. The next day, a different kind of person arrived, and each day thereafter, the people were unlike the last. This continued for over forty days, with guests arriving without end, until the king’s kitchens were exhausted.

The king was greatly alarmed and said to his attendants: “This is some demonic trickery—he cannot be an ordinary man. What is to be done? Kill him!” His attendants replied: “It can be done!”

In the city’s marketplace, they piled firewood and set it ablaze. If he did not die, they would take a great stone to strike his head and cast him into the sea—would he then remain undying?

The Hu king commanded every household in his realm to bring a bundle of firewood, which they heaped in the marketplace and set alight. Laozi and Yin Xi were placed atop the pyre by the Hu king. The prince lit the fire below, and it burned for over forty days until the wood was consumed and the flames died out. Yet Laozi and Yin Xi sat amid the embers, reciting scriptures as before.

The king then had Laozi and Yin Xi bound with great stones and cast into the deep abyss, but again they did not sink. The Hu king was struck with terror. What was to be done now? The entire kingdom trembled in fear, desiring to attend Laozi as their master.

Laozi said to the king: “I am not the master. The one who was burned with me atop the pyre—that is the master. He has now gone to the heavens to summon troops and will come to punish your kingdom for your earlier attempt to burn and kill us.”

In an instant, the armies of the heavenly spirits descended—hundreds of thousands strong, each standing fourteen feet tall, wielding iron staves. They filled the kingdom, arriving without end each day, intent on slaying Jingzi and the king himself. The Hu king was seized with terror, and the thirty-six nations all lost their souls. The king prostrated himself, face to the earth, not daring to look upon Laozi.

Laozi then transformed into a mighty five-colored figure, his body sixteen feet tall, adorned with the seventy-two marks, his radiant purple countenance manifest in the empty sky, moving left and right, now descending, now ascending—this was the form of the *Shifang Kong’er Xu Shen*.

The Hu king, trembling in fear, said to his attendants: “Bring forth the one we held before—this great being!”

Laozi, knowing his intent to submit, replied: “This is no great being, but one known as the Supreme Perfected. The true perfected ones cherish life and abhor killing. I came to your kingdom without transgressing against you—why then did you heap firewood to burn me? And now, what is this desire to attend me? Do you seek escape?”

The Hu king said: “Grant me life, save my kingdom. I pledge my life and heart to you, O great one. From this day forth, I swear never to transgress against you.”

Laozi said: “What will you offer as proof?”

The king replied:

The men and women of my kingdom, young and old, shall never marry, but serve the Master until death, beseeching forgiveness for my sins.”

Thereupon, he summoned the princes of the thirty-six Hu states. Before Laozi, they all shaved their heads and beards, disfiguring their appearance, wearing skirts with the right arm bared, pledging to heaven as witness and swearing upon the earth. With hands clasped and palms joined, they dared not shift or alter their stance.

Seeing the Hu submit to transformation, Laozi then composed a scripture of sixty-four myriad words, the unsurpassed and orthodox Dao of true perfection. He commanded the king to have his entire kingdom follow its laws: they must not raid nests or break eggs, harm any living thing, commit robbery or theft, bully the weak, utter curses or slander, drink wine or eat meat, or engage in reckless speech or double-tongued deceit. They were forbidden to ride in carriages or on horses, or to wear sandals or shoes. He fashioned for them a tin staff, so that when struck against the ground, it would startle insects and prevent them from being harmed.

Fearing they might relapse and regret, he also made for them the three robes of the Dharma, leaving the left arm bare while the right arm was always bound before the heart, the right hand gripping it to prevent the mind from straying. He forbade them from tilling the soil or carving wood, instead providing a begging bowl to hold seven *sheng*. They were to beg for food in accordance with the movements of the sun and moon, receiving one *sheng* from each household. After visiting seven households, they would have seven *sheng*, and upon receiving it, they were to eat. If they failed to obtain food after seven households, they were to reproach themselves. If they went seven days without food, they were to drink only water. This was established as the rule.

The *Scripture on Transforming the Barbarians* originally comprised two scrolls with differing content. Here, their discrepancies have been reconciled, and this text is recorded accordingly.

*Timely Observances* Section.

The Most High Lord of the Great One expounds in the *Mysterious Clouds of the Cavernous Truth*: "Those who ascend at dawn in broad daylight do so when the sun is at its zenith—this is ‘broad daylight’—or at the first crow of the cock, which is ‘ascending at dawn.’" The *Scripture of Illuminating Truth* states: "One who attains transcendence ascends at dawn in broad daylight—this is the meaning." All such moments are chosen for their vital qi.

The *Explication of the Controller of Destiny* says: "Departure in broad daylight is called the ‘upper corpse-liberation.’ Departure at midnight is called the ‘lower corpse-liberation.’ Departure at dawn or dusk is called ‘becoming a master beneath the earth.’"

The *First Scripture of Ascending Mystery* states: "The six periods—dawn, midday, sunset, first watch, midnight, and cockcrow—are times to pay reverence to the Heavenly Worthies of the ten directions, beginning with the east."

The *Hidden Writ of Jade Purity* says: "The days of *jiazi* and the eight solar nodes are all times for the upper court’s morning audience and feast."

The *Scripture of Soaring through the Eight Luminaries* states:
- On the day of *Lichun* (Beginning of Spring), the Three Primordial Ladies of Pure Simplicity ascend to the Celestial August Thearch for a feast—this is the day to practice the Dao of the Primordial Luminance and receive transcendence.
- On the day of *Chunfen* (Spring Equinox), the Heavenly Thearch of the Grand Tenuity ascends to the Highest Jade Sovereign for a feast—this is the day to begin practicing the Dao of the Nascent Luminance and receive transcendence.
- On the day of *Lixia* (Beginning of Summer), the Three Primordial Perfected of the Great Ultimate ascend to the Purple Tenuity Palace for a feast—this is the day to practice the Dao of the Mysterious Luminance and receive transcendence.
- On the day of *Xiazhi* (Summer Solstice), the Duke of Fusang, the Great Thearch, ascends to the Grand Tenuity Palace for a feast—this is the day to practice the Dao of the Void Luminance and receive transcendence.
- On the day of *Liqiu* (Beginning of Autumn), the White Thearch of the Primordial Simplicity ascends to the Jade Heaven and the Highest Perfected of the Mysterious August for a feast—this is the day to practice the Dao of the Primordial Luminance and receive transcendence.
- On the day of *Qiufen* (Autumn Equinox), the Red Thearch of the Southern Culmen ascends to the Terrace of Soaring Winds to feast with the Lady of the Nine Numina—this is the day to practice the Dao of the Radiant Luminance and receive transcendence.
- On the day of *Lidong* (Beginning of Winter), the Perfected of Highest Purity, the August Ancestor Thearch, ascends to the Highest Nine Heavens to feast with the Jade Emperor’s Son—this is the day to practice the Dao of the Cavernous Luminance and receive transcendence.
- On the day of *Dongzhi* (Winter Solstice), the Jade Consort of the Great Empyrean and the Perfected of the Great Void ascend to the Palace of the Great August to feast with the Heavenly Thearch of the Grand Tenuity—this is the day to practice the Dao of the Pure Luminance and receive transcendence.

This has been recorded in advance. The full account appears in the *Section on the Eight Solar Nodes’ Days of Fasting* in the ninth scroll of the *Daoist Precedents*.

**Scroll Nine of the *Three Caverns’ Pearl-Sacred Treasury* Concludes**
**Scroll Ten of the *Three Caverns’ Pearl-Sacred Treasury***
*Compiled by Wang Xuanhe, the Feathered Guest of the Vast Sea of Tang*

**Chapter on Knocking Teeth and Swallowing Saliva**

The *Golden Script and Jade Characters of the Upper Canon* states: At night before sleep, always silently knock the teeth three times seven, and swallow saliva three times seven.

The secret invocation reads:
*"Nine Stars, Great Essence,
North Culmen Perfected Lord,
Augment my essence-womb,
Fortify my three hun-souls.
Draw the sun’s radiance from the left,
Gather the moon’s essence from the right.
At the hour of the Yellow Splendor,
Primal Void’s Yellow Perfected,
Let me ascend as a flying immortal,
Mounting the purple mist.
The Jade Talisman of the Spirit-Void
Ever guards the Gate of Life—
Myriad evils submit to the law,
Receiving form from the Dipper Lord."*

At dawn upon rising, always silently knock the teeth two times seven, and swallow saliva two times seven.

The secret invocation reads:
*"Heaven’s Primal One,
Seven Lads within the Dipper,
Purple Essence of the Upper Clarity,
Dwell within my body.
Flowering Morn’s Purple Canopy,
Mystic Palace of the Great Simplicity,
The Sacred Qi of Later Sages
Descends into the Grotto-Chamber—
Let me ascend as a flying immortal,
Attain the Golden Hall of the Great Ultimate."*

The *Five Talismans* states:
*"Bowing to rinse the fivefold flowery liquid,
Restore the youthful countenance.
Raising to draw the essence of the Three Luminaries,
Preserve the body in eternal peace."*

Knocking the teeth summons the spirits; swallowing qi harmonizes the true. Inhaling harmony and swallowing the six fluids to circulate them, regulating the spirits requires sounding the drum to marshal their ranks—this is called "calling the spirits."

The *Declarations of the Perfected*, Scroll Five, states: When walking at night, one should always click the teeth—there is no fixed number, for it slays demonic and perverse forces. Demons constantly fear the sound of clicking teeth, and thus dare not assail one. If combined with rinsing saliva and reciting invocations, it is even better.

The immortal Liu Jing told Huangfu Long: Upon rising in the morning before washing, sit upright, rinse the mouth’s spittle as "jade spring," let it fill the mouth, then swallow it, knocking the teeth two times seven to conclude. Then rinse and spit again as before, and knock the teeth again in the same manner. Knocking the teeth summons the spirits within the body, settling them, and also prevents the teeth from decaying. Swallowing saliva makes the body lustrous and moist, strengthens vigor and complexion, expels the Three Corpses worms, and is called "refining essence," enabling longevity. If practiced throughout life, one attains immortality.

The *Scripture of the Cavern-Spirit’s Hidden Writ of the Supreme* states: Those who study the Dao must sound the Heavenly Drum to summon the host of spirits. In the practice of right contemplation, to prevent the encroachment of perverse qi, one must assemble the multitude of spirits for self-assistance.

Knocking the left side is the Heavenly Bell; knocking the right side is the Heavenly Chime; knocking the center above and below in opposition is the Heavenly Drum. Sometimes thirty-six knocks correspond to the thirty-six heavens, the thirty-six states in the middle, and the thirty-six lands below. Or thirty-two knocks correspond to the thirty-two heavens; or twenty-seven knocks correspond to the nine heavens’ three-times-nine count, totaling twenty-seven. Or twenty-four knocks correspond to the three-times-eight twenty-four spirits; or twelve knocks correspond to the twelve earthly branches; or nine knocks correspond to the nine origins; or seven knocks correspond to the seven origins; or three knocks correspond to the three origins. Knock according to the number’s correspondence.

If suddenly encountering inauspicious omens, strike the Heavenly Bell thirty times. When traversing mountains to repel evil, recite mighty invocations and strike the Heavenly Chime. When meditating on the Dao to summon spirits, sound the Heavenly Drum. Obstruction in swallowing disrupts the mind’s focus; thus, one must swallow saliva to irrigate the hundred spirits, then tranquilly guard the Three Ones’ spirits. The number of swallows corresponds to the same counts as sounding the Heavenly Drum.

The *Hidden Instructions for Ascending Perfection*, Scroll Four, states: Ingest the Jade Maiden’s saliva, visualizing the sun and moon within the mouth—the sun’s color is red, the moon’s yellow; the sun has nine rays of purple light, the moon ten rays of white light. The rays are straight as strings, entering the mouth; swallow the luminous liquid, practicing this endlessly in secret.

Earlier methods of ingestion all include this swallowing of saliva.

The *Declarations of the Perfected*, Scroll Five, citing the *Great Simplicity’s Scripture of the Cinnabar Splendor*, states: On the face, always rub the hands until warm, then stroke upward and downward following the contours, pressing thoroughly to make the face lustrous and prevent wrinkles and blemishes. Practicing this for five years, one’s complexion becomes like a maiden’s. First rub the palms until hot, then stroke the face and eyes; comb the hair with the hands as if arranging a hairpin. Alternate the arms, rubbing them with the hands to prevent hair from whitening and veins from protruding.

The *Essential Splendor Massage Chapter of the Scripture of the Great Cavern* states: Upon rising from sleep, sit upright and regulate the breath. First clasp the hands, then cover the back of the neck, tilt the head back to gaze upward, and make the neck compete with the hands three or four times to harmonize essence and circulate blood, preventing wind-qi from entering. Long practice averts death and illness. Afterward, flex the body, extend the limbs to the four extremes, arch backward, and shake all joints three times each.

Upon rising, first use a hand towel or thick cloth to wipe the neck on all sides and behind the ears until smooth and warm. Stroke the hair and massage the neck as if arranging a hairpin, without ceasing. After a while, rub the hands and massage the face and eyes. Long practice brightens the eyes, repels perverse qi, and prevents the body from becoming greasy and foul. When finished, swallow saliva thirty times to guide the inner fluids.

The *Scripture of Subduing Demons and Ascending Spirits* states: If the body feels unwell, press the tongue against the throat, rinse and swallow saliva endlessly. Soon, the discomfort will vanish, and one will feel the body relaxed and supple.

The *Upper Scroll of the Scripture of Subduing Demons* states: Frequently press and rub the ears on both sides, alternating without count, to sharpen hearing.

The so-called "nurturing and governing the city walls" is recorded in the *Imperial Register*. It further states: Press the nose on both sides without count, to balance one’s qi. This is called "irrigating the Central Marchmount" and is recorded in the *Emperor’s Record*.

The *Upper Scripture of the Supreme Record of Serene Florescence* on massage methods: At the time of living qi, swallow saliva fourteen times. When finished, press the painful areas of the body, face the sovereign, and recite: *"Left Mysterious, Right Mysterious, the Three Spirits unite as one. Left Yellow, Right Yellow, the Six Flowers harmonize. Wind qi and malignant illnesses retreat to the four directions. Jade fluid flows with luster, ascending and descending freely; within, it dispels water and fire, without, it repels misfortune. Long life and flying transcendence—may the body be at peace and strong."* When finished, swallow saliva fourteen times. Practicing this regularly will prevent illness. Press the painful area thirty-one times without delay.

The *Scripture of the Three and Five in Crimson and Purple* states: When seated, one should often close the eyes and inwardly observe the five viscera and intestines. With long practice, they will naturally become distinct and clear.

The *Scripture of Red Characters on Stone* states: Often cover the mouth and nose with the hands, gaze inward, and gently breathe. After a while, saliva will form in the hands; use it to massage the face and eyes. Regular practice makes the body fragrant.

The *Purple Radiance of Blazing Light Scripture: Inner Vision Method* states: Often close the eyes and lie down, settle the body, and breathe gently, as if asleep, so that others do not notice. Then inwardly gaze and listen to the four directions, directing the ears and eyes to ten thousand *li* beyond. With long practice, one will naturally see things ten thousand *li* away. With focused intent, one may see a hundred thousand *li* beyond. The ears will also constantly hear the sounds of gold and jade, strings and bamboo—this is a wondrous method.

The *Scripture of the Three Celestial Passes* states: Often press the areas near the nose beside the eyes with the hands, pausing when the qi flows through, then exhale and begin again. Regular practice enables penetrating vision.

The Dao states: Often press the small cavities behind the eyebrows thirty-six times, then rub the face above the eyes with the palms and fingers. Rotate the ears thirty times, massaging frequently without fixed intervals. When finished, stroke the forehead upward thirty-six times, beginning between the eyebrows and moving into the hairline. Swallow saliva as much as desired without count. Regular practice brightens the eyes, allowing one to read at night within a year. This may also be done discreetly at the philtrum without speaking of its method. The downward pressure beneath the eyes is the secret to preserving the eyes and returning to the infant’s Dao. Rotating the ears with the hands is the technique of "probing brightness and reflection." Thus, the blood flows and disperses, wrinkles do not form, and the moon’s radiance and mysterious illumination harmonize essence and spirit. When a person grows old, it rarely does not begin with the ears and eyes. The signs of aging also first appear beside the eyes. Press the forehead, inwardly visualize the Red Child and the twin luminaries of sun and moon, rejoicing in the Upper Prime, thirty-six times beginning at the eyebrows. This is called "the hands paying homage to the Three Primes," the Dao of fortifying the brain and strengthening the hair. Cover the four sides of the head with both hands, smoothing the hair toward the topknot, as much as possible. Thus, the blood of the head flows and disperses, and wind-dampness does not congeal. When finished, press the four corners of the eyes thirty-six times until the light is clearly seen—this is the method of refining the eye spirits. With long practice, one may see the hundred spirits. Diligently practicing this, keeping the hands never far from the face, is best. Even after attaining transcendence, one should not abandon it. Upon waking at night, always knock the teeth nine times, swallow saliva nine times, then press the sides of the nose up and down dozens of times. Softly recite: *"The Four Luminaries of the Supreme, the Nine Gates emit essence. Ears and eyes profoundly clear, communicating with the real and reaching the numinous. The Terrace of Heaven’s Center, flowing qi harmonized. The Cloudy Maid’s graceful bearing, the Eye Lad’s brilliance. Flowering hearing and radiant clarity, the hundred arts subtly refined. Preserving and uniting the Upper Prime, wandering the Nine Cities. The five viscera take root, ears and eyes naturally arise. The Heavenly Terrace’s pure simplicity, its pillars and beams unshaken. The seven *po* refined, the three *hun* at peace. The Red Child carries the light, ever accompanying me. Should any dare obscure my ears and eyes, the Supreme will crush them with flowing bells. The ten thousand evils vanish, all wishes are fulfilled. Sun and moon guard the gates, the heart stores the five stars. The True Sovereign’s incantation—let all echoes heed with reverence."*

The *Declarations of the Perfected* states: When combing the hair, do so many times to circulate the blood and qi and disperse wind-dampness. Frequently change combs, alternating their use. One need not undo the hair.

The *Scripture of the Great Ultimate’s Verdant Radiance* states: When combing the hair, face the sovereign’s direction. At the beginning of combing, softly recite: *"Mysterious Flower of the Mud-Pellet, preserving essence and ensuring its long abiding. Left as the Hidden Moon, right as the Root of the Sun. The Six Harmonies purified, the hundred spirits receive grace."* When finished, swallow saliva three times. Regular practice prevents hair loss and promotes daily growth. Frequently change combs, combing thoroughly without causing pain. One may also have an attendant comb the hair thoroughly. Thus, the blood and fluids do not stagnate, and the hair roots remain firm. Before sleeping at night, first tightly close the eyes upward, then press and wipe with the backs of the thumbs, crossing both palms at the crown of the head thirty-six times. Inwardly visualize three colored qi—purple, cyan, and crimson—emerging before the eyes. This is the inner pressing of the Three Primordial Clouds, irrigating and uniting with the Lad. Secretly recite: *"Eye Lad of the Three Clouds, True Lords of the Two Eyes. Brilliance infuses essence, opening and clearing the pure spirit. The Supreme Mystery’s numinous bearing, the graceful and soaring Numinous Maid. Preserving the double passes, unlocking the Nine Gates. The hundred joints respond in harmony, morning fluids irrigate the Mud-Pellet. The body ascends to the Jade Palace, ranked among the Upper Perfected."*

These forty-eight characters recited, swallow saliva fifty times. When finished, then open the eyes. Make this a regular practice—it may be performed sitting or rising, not limited to night, but must be done at the time of generative qi. After a year, ears and eyes will become keen and bright. With long practice, one may see through a thousand li, perceive the radiance of spirits, and hear beyond silence. This is indeed a lofty Dao of the perfected immortals, not merely for brightening eyes and opening ears.

Those who wish to study the Dao should strive to keep their affairs concealed from others, as Master Meng transmitted in seclusion. Before sleeping at night, first recite the *Huangting Neijing Jing* once, then sleep, so that the hun and po souls may be refined and restrained. If practiced constantly for twenty-one years, one may attain immortality. This is said to require ten thousand recitations—three or four each evening is excellent. Lady Jiang of the Northern Peak said: reciting this scripture also keeps one free from illness. It is the Dao of not dying. A note says: reciting it once each evening for twenty-one years does not reach ten thousand. The character "one" may be a corruption for "seven" or "eight." Otherwise, three or four recitations per evening suffice.

Whenever studying the profound Dao or reciting sacred scriptures, for every ten or twenty words, one should once or twice lick the lips and swallow saliva; for every fifty or a hundred words, two or three times knock the teeth, to harmonize spirit with the numinous origin, regulate blood and qi, and condense the subtle fluids until they fill the abode of the Supreme Unity. This is what is meant by "the qi flows without labor, the blood does not leak."

In the method for students, one must not weep tears or spit excessively, for these deplete the fluids and leak the essence, causing the throat and brain to burn dry. Thus, perfected persons and Daoist adepts constantly practice exhalation, inhalation, and swallowing to harmonize the six fluids.

On the day of one’s natal sign, face its direction, knock the teeth three times, and silently bow twice while reciting: *"The Supreme Unity governs life, the Three Qi unite with the true. The womb-chamber ascends to the Upper Radiance, mother mysterious and father primordial. They give birth to my five viscera, gather my spirit. Below, they irrigate the Jade Fluid; above, they ascend to the Mud-Pellet. At dusk, refine the seven po; at dawn, harmonize the three hun. On the right, command the Jade Splendor; on the left, summon the Golden Dawn. Let me become a spirit immortal, commanding the numinous and employing the divine. Constantly preserve the beneficent fluids, soaring through the Ten Heavens."* When finished, silently bow to the four directions and knock the teeth three more times. This is called the Dao of the Supreme Lord’s "Concealed Morning Audience of the Womb-Origin." Practicing it constantly secures the hun and po souls, ensuring long life and immortality.

*The Declarations of the Perfected, Scroll Eight* states: Long ago, there was a man named Bao Zhu from Jibei. He neither studied the Dao nor knew any methods or arts. At over forty years of age, he suddenly contracted a wind affliction that twisted his mouth and eyes, causing his upper and lower teeth to constantly clatter together with a loud sound, day and night without cease. He lived to be 127 years old, and later perished by falling into the Longevity River during a great flood. The Northern Emperor had repeatedly sent demon-slayers and the Day-Wandering Earth Calamity Envoys to take him, yet these executioners dared not approach. The demon officials questioned the reason, and the celestial slayer replied: "This man employed many methods to restrain his ordinary state, knocking his teeth and sounding the Celestial Drum to alert the spirits within his body. The spirits could not scatter, and demonic qi could not enter, so there was no opportunity to kill him." By this reasoning, had Bao Zhu not crossed the river by water, he might have lived a thousand years—his lifespan was not yet exhausted. It was merely an accident of extreme cold; stepping into the water, his mouth clenched and he could no longer knock his teeth, thus meeting his fate by drowning.

Those afflicted with wind disease whose teeth chatter of their own accord still repel death and ward off demon-slayers—how much more so for Daoist adepts who truly knock their teeth and sound the Celestial Drum to summon the spirits of the body!

The *Immortal Methods* states: constantly swallowing saliva and knocking the teeth makes one return to youth. The *Purple Radiance of Blazing Light Scripture* says: swallowing saliva preserves the complexion and protects the teeth. The highest method for seeking immortality states: at the dawn hour when the Two Qi have not yet divided, let the mysterious radiance illumine body and spirit. Body and spirit descend together, ascending to meet the Mud-Pellet, and essence and fluids are generated. Swallowing at this time, after three years the face will glow with jade-like luster, the countenance will transform, the neck’s radiance will be firmly rooted, and the teeth will grow square and even. With constant cultivation, the Five Elders will descend to one’s chamber, and the spirit immortal will ascend to the Mysterious. Lifespan will equal the Three Luminaries. This is the Dao of not dying—do not transmit it to the unworthy.

At that time, calm the mind and settle the intent, still the five spirits, knock the teeth twelve times, and visualize the Azure Maiden of the Eastern Essence, bearing the qi of Lesser Yang, the Jade Nectar of Azure Mushrooms, irrigating and rinsing one’s body, flowing and overflowing within the Purple Tenuity Palace. Recite: *"Azure Teeth of the East, drink the morning radiance. Jade nectar and sweet springs, cascading fluids in torrents. Flowing to moisten the six palaces, the mysterious infusion like a river. The body light, ascending to tread the Supreme Rosy Clouds."* When finished, with the tongue lick the outer side of the upper teeth nine times and swallow.

Next, visualize the Vermilion Maiden of the Southern Round Jade, bearing the qi of Greater Yang, the Jade Nectar of Crimson Mushrooms, irrigating one’s body and flowing into the Crimson Palace. Recite: *"Vermilion Teeth of the South, drink the sweet springs and crimson mushroom jade nectar. Flowing and overflowing like a river, spreading moisture through the Crimson Palace. The bones transform and generate spirit, consuming the Great Void. The entire body becomes immortal, riding clouds and driving the dawn, ascending to stand before the Emperor."* When finished, with the tongue lick the outer side of the lower teeth eight times and swallow.

Next, visualize the Pristine Maiden of the West, bearing the qi of Lesser Yin and the Jade Nectar of White Mushrooms, irrigating one’s body and flowing into the Canopy Palace. Recite: *"White Teeth of the West, drink the numinous fluid. Jade water in mighty flow, the mysterious mushrooms resplendent. Irrigate my six palaces, secure the hun and solidify the po. The spirit rests in the stomach duct, the name inscribed in the Golden Register."* When finished, with the tongue lick the inner side of the upper teeth six times and swallow.

Next, visualize the Mysterious Maiden of the North, bearing the qi of Greater Yin and the Jade Water of Black Mushrooms, irrigating one’s body and flowing into the Great Granary Palace.

Recite: *"Black Teeth of the North, consume the mysterious essence, drink my flying spring, nourish me with jade sweetness. The spirit’s palace shines resplendent, like cinnabar, like mushrooms. Lifespan rivals heaven and earth, boundless as the aeons."* When finished, with the tongue lick the inner side of the lower teeth five times and swallow.

Next, visualize the Yellow Pristine Maiden of the Center, bearing the qi of Central Harmony and the Elixir of Yellow Water and Moonlight, irrigating one’s body and flowing into the Jade Hall Palace. Recite: *"Yellow Teeth of the Center, white stones towering. When hungry, consume the elixir of jade sweetness; when thirsty, drink the Yellow Water and Moonlight. The five viscera overflow, flowing and moistening like a river. Lifespan equals the Three Dawns, ten thousand without decay. Form ascends to the Nine Mysteries, controlling and riding the flying clouds."* When finished, with the tongue lick the inner and outer sides of the upper and lower teeth on all four surfaces, then press the tongue against the Mysterious Throat, drawing the mushroom fluid twelve times and swallowing.

The method of swallowing fluid to preserve the teeth is what the Central Yellow Venerable Lord and the Perfected of the Great Ultimate constantly cultivate. Their complexion is like that of a youth, their skin like jade’s luster, their body full and qi abundant. Their white hair returns to black, their teeth take root firmly, without rot or loss. Thus they attain the descent of the mysterious, their names inscribed in the Immortal Registers, their rank ascending to the Pure Void, sharing the Emperor’s seat. If you cultivate this, you shall seek your name in the Golden Portal. Without the karmic affinity of the Jade Pavilion, one cannot unravel these mysteries.

The *Inner Sounds and Jade Scriptures, Upper Scroll* states: *"With the tongue stir the upper, lower, and center of the mouth, filling it with jade fluid, then swallow three times—this grants longevity and extends life."* If one serves the Blue Teeth of the East, consuming the Blue Teeth and drinking the Morning Flower, when finished, with the tongue stir the inner side of the upper teeth, lick the lips three times, fill the mouth with jade spring, and swallow. Here ends the tenth scroll of the *Three Caverns’ Pearl Bag*.
